Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
12 min
Proof that the Imperative Indicates Obligation: Consensus and Reason
Commentary on proofs for imperative indicating obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the proofs of consensus (ijma) and rational argument (ma'qul) to establish that the imperative form (amr) indicates obligation (wujub), and identify the Hanafi position in the usul dispute.

Core Idea
The imperative indicates obligation by consensus and reason, not by mere linguistic assumption.

This commentary passage expands on the matn's claim that the imperative form (sigha al-amr) indicates obligation (wujub) when free from contextual clues. It addresses a potential objection and presents two proofs: consensus (ijma) of scholars and a rational argument (ma'qul). Understanding these proofs is essential for grasping how Hanafi usul derives binding commands from the Qur'an and Sunnah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim and objection
The passage first addresses an objection that the imperative might indicate mere censure (inkar) rather than obligation. Note how the commentary uses context to refute this.
The phrase 'على وجه الإنكار دون الترك' indicates the objection.
2
Analyze the consensus proof
The passage states that scholars have agreed (ajma'u) that anyone who wants to request an action only uses the imperative word. Perfection in request is obligation, and the default is that words are not shared (ishtirak) between meanings. Thus, the imperative must indicate obligation.
The consensus is not directly on the ruling but on the usage pattern.
3
Analyze the rational proof
Verbs like past, present, and future each have specific meanings. Similarly, the imperative should have a specific meaning, which is obligation. Another rational proof: if a master commands his slave and the slave disobeys, the slave deserves punishment, which would not happen if the imperative did not indicate obligation.
The rational proof is not qiyas in language but establishes negation of sharing.
4
Address the potential criticism
The commentator clarifies that this reasoning does not establish language through analogy (qiyas) but rather proves that the original principle is negation of linguistic sharing (asl 'adam al-ishtirak). This refutes the objection that linguistic matters cannot be proven rationally.
This step shows the sophistication of Hanafi usul in defending linguistic principles.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان موجب الأمر على وجه الإنكار دون الترك، والجواب: أن سياق الكلام دال على أن هذا الأمر للوجوب بدون احتياج إلى برهان ومصادرة على المطلوب، وأن المخالفة في استعمالهم إنما تطلق على ترك العمل به فتأمّل. ولدلالة الإجماع والمعقول عطف على ما قبله وفي بعض النسخ: وكذا دلالة الإجماع والمعقول يدلان عليه فحينئذٍ هو جملة مستقلة معطوفة على مضمون سابقها، وحاصله: أن دلالة الإجماع تدل على أن الأمر للوجوب؛ لأنهم أجمعوا على أن كل من أراد أن يطلب فعلاً من أحد لا يطلب إلا بلفظ الأمر، والكمال في الطلب هو الوجوب، والأصل نفي الاشتراك فتعين أن موجبه الوجوب، وإنما قال: دلالة الإجماع؛ لأن نفس الإجماع لم ينعقد على أن موجبه الوجوب؛ لأنه مختلف فيه بل إنما الإجماع على شيء يدل عليه، وكذا الدليل المعقول يدل على أن الأمر للوجوب، وهو أن تصاريف الأفعال كلها كالماضي والمستقبل، والحال دال على معنى مخصوص، فينبغي أن يكون الأمر دالاً على معنى الوجوب، وليس هذا لإثبات اللغة بالقياس بل لإثبات كون الأصل عدم الاشتراك، وقيل: المعقول هو أن السيد إذا أمر غلامه بفعل و لم يفعل استحق العقاب، فلو لم يكن الأمر للوجوب لما استحق ذلك، وقد نقل في بيان النصوص والمعقول لا يطلب إلخ لأنه لا يجد لفظًا يظهر مقصوده سوى الأمر، فهذا يدل على أن المطلوب منه الوجود، ولا وجود إلا بالوجوب (السنبلي) والكمال في الطلب إلخ فإن كمال الطلب إنما يكون إذا لم يرخص الطالب ترك المأمور به ؛ إذ لو رخص لم يكن طالبًا من كل وجه ولا قصور في صيغة ولا في ولاية المتكلم، فإنه مفترض الطاعة، فيملك الإلزام الكامل. (القمر) والأصل نفي الاشتراك فإن اللفظ إذا دار بين الاشتراك والحقيقة والمجاز يحمل على الحقيقة والمجاز. (القمر) مختلف فيه أي بين الأئمة المجتهدين. (القمر) على شيء وهو أن كل من أراد أن يطلب فعلاً من أحد لا يطلب إلا بلفظ الأمر عليه أي على أن موجب الأمر الوجوب. (القمر) على معنى مخصوص: لا يوجد إلا في ذلك اللفظ الموضوع له فالماضي يدل على المضي، والمستقبل على الاستقبال، والحال على الحال فينبغي إلخ. (القمر) وليس هذا إلخ: دفع دخل مقدر تقريره: أن كون موجب الأمر للوجوب أمر لغوي، وقد أثبتموه بالمعقول، فصار هذا الدليل لإثبات اللغة بالقياس وهو غير جائز، وحاصل الدفع: أن هذا ليس لإثبات اللغة بالقياس، بل لإثبات كون الأصل عدم الاشتراك، فإن كلاً من الماضي والمستقبل والحال دال على معنى خاص ليس مشتركا، فكذا الأمر لا يكون مشتركًا. (القمر) في بيان النصوص والمعقول إلخ بيان النص والمعقول نقله في حاشية "قمر الأقمار" وأذكر لك مثالاً آخر للمعقول لم يذكره في الحاشية المذكورة، وهو أن الإيجاب معنى مقصود فلابد له من لفظ يخصه. (السنبلي)
Explanation of what the imperative necessitates (obligation) on the basis of [it being] for censure, not for leaving [the act]; and the answer: that the context of speech indicates that this imperative is for obligation without needing a proof and without begging the question; and that 'opposition' in their usage is only applied to leaving off acting upon it, so reflect. And 'by the indication of consensus and reason' is a conjunction to what preceded it, and in some copies: 'likewise the indication of consensus and reason both indicate it'; then it is an independent clause conjoined to the content of its preceding [clause], and its summary: that the indication of consensus indicates that the imperative is for obligation, because they unanimously agreed that whoever wants to request an action from someone does not request except with the word of command, and perfection in request is obligation, and the original principle is negation of [linguistic] sharing, thus it is determined that its necessitation is obligation. He only said 'indication of consensus' because the consensus itself was not concluded that its necessitation is obligation, since there is disagreement about it; rather the consensus is upon something that indicates it. Likewise the rational proof indicates that the imperative is for obligation, and that is that all the conjugations of verbs, like past, future, and present, indicate a particular meaning, so the imperative should indicate the meaning of obligation. And this is not to establish language through analogy, but rather to establish that the original principle is negation of sharing. And it is said: the rational argument is that if a master commands his slave to do something and he does not do it, he deserves punishment; for if the imperative were not for obligation, he would not deserve that. And it has been transmitted in 'Bayān al-Nuṣūṣ wa al-Ma'qūl' that he does not request [except] because he does not find a word to express his intent except the imperative; this indicates that what is required is existence, and existence is only through obligation. (al-Sanbalī) 'And perfection in request...' for the perfection of request is only when the requester does not permit leaving the commanded act; for if he permitted, he would not be a requester in every respect, and there is no deficiency in the verbal form nor in the authority of the speaker, for he is one whose obedience is obligatory, so he possesses complete power to obligate. (al-Qamar) 'And the original principle is negation of sharing': for if a word is ambiguous between sharing and literal/figurative meanings, it is interpreted as literal and figurative. (al-Qamar) 'Disagreed about': i.e., among the imams of ijtihad. (al-Qamar) 'Upon something': i.e., that whoever wants to request an action from someone does not request except with the word of command; upon it i.e., that the imperative necessitates obligation. (al-Qamar) 'Upon a particular meaning': it does not exist except in that word coined for it; thus the past indicates pastness, the future indicates futuricity, and the present indicates presentness; therefore it should be so. (al-Qamar) 'And this is not...': a refutation of a potential objection whose gist is: that the imperative's indicating obligation is a linguistic matter, and you have proven it through reason, so this proof becomes establishing language through analogy, which is impermissible. The gist of the refutation: that this is not for establishing language through analogy, but rather for establishing that the original principle is negation of sharing; for each of the past, future, and present indicates a specific meaning that is not shared, so likewise the imperative is not shared. (al-Qamar) 'In 'Bayān al-Nuṣūṣ wa al-Ma'qūl'...': the explanation of the textual and rational proofs is quoted in the hashia of 'Qamar al-Aqmār', and I provide another example for the rational that he did not mention in the said hashia: that obligation is an intended meaning, so it must have a word specific to it. (al-Sanbalī)
Source pages p. 79

Commentary
This passage from the commentary on the matn regarding the imperative (amr) is an expansion of the proof that the imperative form (sigha al-amr) indicates obligation (wujub) when free from contextual clues. The author addresses an objection that the imperative might be used for censure (inkar) rather than obligation, but responds that the context shows it is for obligation. He then introduces two proofs: consensus (ijma') and rational argument (ma'qul). The proof from consensus is that scholars have consistently used the imperative to request actions in a way that implies obligation, and no one requests an action except using the word of command, with perfection in request being obligation. The rational proof is that verbs have specific meanings (past, future, present), so the imperative should likewise indicate a specific meaning, which is obligation. The author clarifies that this is not establishing language through analogy (qiyas), but rather establishing that the original principle is negation of linguistic sharing (asl 'adam al-ishtirak). The objection that this would be qiyas in language is refuted. Another rational proof is given: if a master commands his slave and the slave disobeys, the slave deserves punishment; this would not be the case if the imperative did not indicate obligation. The passage also notes that consensus is not directly on the necessity of obligation, but on something that indicates it. The commentary by al-Qamar and al-Sanbali further explain these points, emphasizing that the imperative's indication is established through these proofs, not by mere linguistic assumption.

Key Terms
الأمر (al-amr): The imperative verbal form (sigha) used to request an action.
الوجوب (al-wujub): Obligation; a legal ruling requiring performance of an act without option to omit.
الإجماع (al-ijma'): Consensus of the scholars of the community on a legal ruling or principle.
المعقول (al-ma'qul): Rational argument or reasoning that leads to a legal conclusion.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what are the two proofs that the imperative indicates obligation?
A) Quran and Sunnah
B) Ijma (consensus) and Ma'qul (reason)
C) Qiyas and Istihsan
D) Urf and Maslaha

Key Takeaway
The imperative form indicates obligation through the dual proofs of consensus (ijma) and rational argument (ma'qul), not by mere linguistic convention.

'Aw' in Agency and Contracts: General Rule and the Istihsan of Khiyar al-Ta'yin
Distinction between 'aw' in agency (valid) and sale/lease (invalid) with khiyar al-ta'yin exception via istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing 'aw' in agency vs sale/lease, and identify when khiyar al-ta'yin is valid by istihsan, explaining the role of the known option holder in removing dispute.

Core Idea
'Aw' in contracts creates uncertainty; agency tolerates it, sale/lease do not, except khiyar al-ta'yin with a known option holder.

The word 'أو' (or) has a different legal effect depending on the contract type. In agency, it grants flexibility; in sale and lease, it introduces uncertainty that normally voids the contract. However, the Hanafi school carves out an exception: when the party holding the option is known and the choice is limited to two or three items, the contract is valid by juristic preference (istihsan). This lesson unpacks that distinction and the usul reasoning behind it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two contexts: agency vs sale/lease
Read the passage and note the ruling for each: in agency, 'aw' makes the appointment valid; in sale/lease, it generally invalidates the contract.
The reason given: agency is built on expansion (tawassu'), so uncertainty is tolerated.
2
Locate the exception: khiyar al-ta'yin
When the option holder (buyer/seller/lessor/lessee) is known and the choice is limited to 2-3 items, the contract is valid by istihsan.
The passage specifies that the ignorance (jahala) does not lead to dispute because the option holder will decide.
3
Analyze the usul reasoning: istihsan over qiyas
The Hanafis use a hidden analogy (qiyas khafi) to khiyar al-shart (option of condition), which is permitted by the Sunnah. This analogy is preferred over strict qiyas (which would invalidate due to uncertainty) because of need and removal of dispute.
This is a classical example of istihsan as a source of law.
4
Compare with opposing view (Zufar/Shafi'i)
Zufar and al-Shafi'i apply strict qiyas: any uncertainty (jahala) invalidates the contract. They do not accept the istihsan exception.
The practical difference: Hanafis enforce the contract after the option is exercised; others consider it void from the start.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The text clearly states that khiyar al-ta'yin is valid by istihsan, and this is the relied-upon Hanafi position.
The passage uses the phrase 'فيصح استحسانًا' (so it is valid by istihsan) indicating the adopted view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإذا دخلت في الوكالة يصح بأن يقول: "وكلت هذا أو هذا فأيهما تصرف صح الوكيلين ولا يشترط اجتماعهما؛ لأن "أو" في موضع الإنشاء للتخيير والتوكيل إنشاء. بخلاف البيع والإجارة ؛ فإنه لا يصح الترديد فيهما بأن يقول: بعت هذا أو هذا أو بعت هذا بألف أو "بألفين وأجرت هذا أو "هذا" أو "آجرت هذا بألف أو بألفين لبقاء المعقود عليه أو المعقود به مجهولاً مع عدم تعين من له الخيار. أي خيار التعيين إلا أن يكون من له الخيار معلومًا في اثنين أو ثلاثة، متعلق بالبيع والإجارة أي لا يصح البيع والإجارة قط إلا أن يكون من له الخيار معلومًا بأن يقول : على أن الخيار فأيهما تصرف صح الوكيلين ولا يشترط اجتماعهما؛ لأن "أو" في موضع الإنشاء للتخيير والتوكيل إنشاء. بخلاف البيع والإجارة ؛ فإنه لا يصح الترديد فيهما بأن يقول: بعت هذا أو هذا أو بعت هذا بألف أو "بألفين وأجرت هذا أو "هذا" أو "آجرت هذا بألف أو بألفين لبقاء المعقود عليه أو المعقود به مجهولاً مع عدم تعين من له الخيار. أي خيار التعيين إلا أن يكون من له الخيار معلومًا في اثنين أو ثلاثة، متعلق بالبيع والإجارة أي لا يصح البيع والإجارة قط إلا أن يكون من له الخيار معلومًا بأن يقول : على أن الخيار والتوكيل إنشاء ومبنى الوكالة على التوسع، فلا يكون الجهالة مفضية إلى المنازعة. (القمر) بعت هذا أو هذا هذا ترديد في المعقود عليه أي المبيع. (القمر) بألف أو بألفين هذا ترديد في المعقود به أي الثمن. (القمر) وأجرت هذا أو هذا هذا ترديد في المعقود عليه أي الشيء المستأجر. (القمر) بألف أو بألفين هذا ترديد في المعقود به أي الأجرة. (القمر) مجهولا : أي جهالة تفضي إلى المنازعة. (القمر) في اثنين أو ثلاثة إلخ : أي يكون المبيع اثنين بأن يقول: بعت هذا أو هذا، أو يكون المبيع ثلاثة بأن يقول: بعت هذا أو هذا أو هذا، أو يكون الثمن اثنين بأن يقول: "بعت هذا على هذا أو هذا، أو ثلاثة كما يقول : "بعت هذا على هذا أو هذا أو هذا إلخ. (السنبلي) بيان أقسام التقسيم الثالث بحث كلمة "أو " في التعيين للبائع أو للمشتري، أو للآجر أو للمستأجر، ويكون الخيار واقعا في اثنين أو ثلاثة من المبيع والثمن ومن الأجرة والدار لا أزيد من الثلاثة؛ لأن الثلاثة تشتمل على الجيد والوسط والردئ، والرابع زائد لا حاجة إليه، والجهالة غير مفضية إلى المنازعة لتعين من له الخيار. فيصح استحسانًا إلحاقا لهذا الخيار بخيار الشرط، وعند زفر والشافعي ما لا يصح أي خيار التعيين قياسًا للجهالة.
And if [the word 'aw'] enters into agency, it is valid, such that he says: 'I appoint this or this as my agent; whichever of them acts, his action is valid' and their joint action is not required, because 'aw' in the context of creation is for choice, and appointment is creation. Unlike sale and lease, for repetition (taraddad) is not valid in them, such as if he says: 'I sold this or this', or 'I sold this for one thousand or two thousand', or 'I leased this or this', or 'I leased this for one thousand or two thousand', because the object of contract or the consideration remains unknown with the lack of specification of the person who has the option. i.e., the option of determination. Except if the person who has the option is known in two or three [matters], related to sale and lease. i.e., sale and lease are not valid at all unless the person who has the option is known, as when he says: 'on condition that I have the option' and agency is creation and the foundation of agency is expansion, so ignorance does not lead to dispute. (al-Qamar) 'I sold this or this' is repetition in the object of contract, i.e., the sold item. (al-Qamar) 'For one thousand or two thousand' is repetition in the consideration, i.e., the price. (al-Qamar) 'And I leased this or this' is repetition in the object of lease, i.e., the leased item. (al-Qamar) 'For one thousand or two thousand' is repetition in the consideration, i.e., the rent. (al-Qamar) 'Unknown' i.e., ignorance that leads to dispute. (al-Qamar) 'In two or three, etc.' i.e., the sold item is two [items] as when he says: 'I sold this or this', or the sold item is three as when he says: 'I sold this or this or this', or the price is two as when he says: 'I sold this for this or this', or three as when he says: 'I sold this for this or this or this, etc.' (al-Sunbuliy) Explanation of the divisions of the third division: Discussion of the word 'aw' regarding specification for the seller or buyer, or for the lessor or lessee, and the option occurs in two or three of the sold item and price, and of the rent and house, not more than three, because three includes the good, medium, and bad; the fourth is superfluous and not needed, and ignorance does not lead to dispute due to the specification of who has the option. So it is valid by istihsan, analogizing this option to the option of condition (khiyar al-shart). And according to Zufar and al-Shafi'i, it is not valid, i.e., the option of determination (khiyar al-ta'yin), by qiyas due to ignorance.
Source pages p. 351

Commentary
This passage contrasts the effect of the word 'أو' in agency versus sale and lease. In agency, using 'أو' is valid because agency is based on flexibility (tawassu'). The principal can say 'I appoint this or this as my agent' and whichever acts, the action is valid. In contrast, in sale and lease, using 'أو' makes the contract invalid because the object or price remains unknown, causing dispute. However, there is an exception: the option of determination (khiyar al-ta'yin). If the person who holds the option (buyer, seller, lessor, lessee) is known and the choice is limited to two or three items (like goods of different qualities), then the contract is valid by istihsan (juristic preference). This is analogized to the option of condition (khiyar al-shart) which is permitted by the Sunnah. The Hanafis hold that the ignorance here does not lead to dispute because the option holder will choose. Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i disagree, arguing by qiyas that the ignorance invalidates the contract. The passage also notes that the choice should be limited to three items because that covers good, medium, and bad, and more is unnecessary.

Key Terms
خيار التعيين (khiyar al-ta'yin): The option to choose one of two or three items in a contract
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that sets aside strict analogy for a stronger hidden analogy or public interest
جهالة مفضية إلى المنازعة (jahala mufdiya ila al-munaza'ah): Ignorance that leads to dispute; invalidates contracts

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafis, why is khiyar al-ta'yin valid in sale and lease despite the ignorance?
A) Because the ignorance is temporary and will be resolved later.
B) Because it is analogized to khiyar al-shart, and the ignorance does not lead to dispute due to the known option holder.
C) Because the contract is conditional on the option exercise.
D) Because all scholars agree on its validity for necessity.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school validates khiyar al-ta'yin by istihsan when the option holder is known and the choice is limited, because the uncertainty does not lead to dispute.

The Fourth Category of Majhul: Mustankar (Rejected by the Salaf)
Defines fourth category with example and ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fourth category of majhul (mustankar) and explain why the hadith of Fatima bint Qays is classified as such, including the role of ijma in its rejection.

Core Idea
A hadith unanimously rejected by the Salaf is mustankar and cannot be acted upon.

In Hanafi usul, not all unknown narrators are treated equally. The fourth category is the mustankar: a hadith that the early scholars (Salaf) explicitly rejected. The classic example is Fatima bint Qays's claim that the Prophet did not give her lodging or maintenance after triple divorce. Umar ibn al-Khattab rejected it publicly, and no Companion objected, establishing a tacit consensus that rendered the hadith objectionable. This lesson unpacks the definition, the evidence, and the scholarly disagreement around this category.

Guided Path
1
Identify the category
The passage states that if the Salaf only rejected a narrator's hadith, it becomes mustankar (objectionable) and not accepted. This is the fourth type of unknown narrator.
Mustankar is a subset of majhul, defined by the reaction of the Salaf.
2
Examine the example
The example is Fatima bint Qays's hadith: her husband divorced her three times, and she claimed the Prophet gave her no lodging or maintenance. Umar rejected this, citing the Quran and his own hearing from the Prophet.
Umar's rejection was based on stronger evidence.
3
Understand the consensus
Umar stated his rejection in the presence of many Companions, and none objected. This silence constitutes a tacit consensus (ijma) that the hadith is mustankar.
Ijma makes the rejection binding in the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the ikhtilaf
Later scholars like Isa ibn Aban and Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi argued that Umar was actually using analogy (qiyas), not rejecting the hadith outright. The text presents both views.
This is a legitimate scholarly difference in interpreting Umar's action.
5
Apply the ruling
Because of the consensus, the Hanafi school does not act on this hadith. Instead, it follows the Quran and Umar's report, which grant the thrice-divorced woman lodging and maintenance (unless pregnant).
The practical fiqh outcome: maintenance is obligatory for the thrice-divorced non-pregnant woman.

Source Text

وإن لم يظهر من السلف إلا الرد كان مستنكرًا، فلا يقبل وهذا هو القسم الرابع من المجهول، ومثاله: ما روت فاطمة بنت قيس لها أن زوجها طلقها ثلاثا، ولم يفرض لها رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم سكنى ولا نفقة وردّه عمر ، وقال : لا ندع كتاب ربنا وسنة نبينا بقول امرأة، لا ندري أصدقت أم كذبت أحفظت أم نسيت فإني سمعت رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم يقول لها النفقة والسكنى. ** وقد قال ذلك عمر ه بمحضر من الصحابة؛ فلم ينكره أحد فكان إجماعًا على أن الحديث مستنكر. ولكن قيل أراد عمر بالكتاب والسنة والقياس على الحامل المبتوتة، وعلى المعتدة عن طلاق رجعي بجامع الاحتباس، وقيل: بين السنة هو بنفسه وأراد بالكتاب قوله تعالى: لا تُخْرِجُوهُنَّ مِنْ بُيُوتِهِنَّ في باب السكنى وقوله: وَلِلْمُطَلَّقَاتِ مَتَاعٌ بِالْمَعْرُوفِ في باب النفقة. وإن لم يظهر ، هذا هو القسم الخامس من المجهول أي إن لم يظهر حديثه في السلف فلم يقابل بردّ ولا قبول يجوز العمل به . فلم ينكره أحد فلم يقبل حديث فاطمة بنت قيس أحد إلا جماعة قليلة منهم ابن عباس، وللأكثر حكم الكل ولكن قيل : القائل عيسى بن أبان أراد عمر: فإن القياس الصحيح ثابت بالكتاب والسنة، فالكتاب والسنة سببا ثبوته، فأطلق اسم السبب وأريد المسبب. أراد عمر إلخ بمناسبة أن القياس أيضًا ثابت بالكتاب والسنة، أما الكتاب فهو قوله تعالى شانه: فَاعْتَبِرُوا يَا أُولِي الْأَبْصَارِ وأما الحديث فهو مشهور، وهو ما روى أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم لما بعث معاذًا إلى اليمن قاضيًا قال : بم تحكم ؟ قال : بكتاب الله قال فإن لم تجد؟ قال : بسنة رسول الله قال فإن لم تجد؟ قال: أجتهد برأيي فصوبه النبي له وقال : الحمد لله الذي وفق رسول رسوله بما يرضاه الله ورسوله. على الحامل المبتوتة البت القطع، والمراد الحامل المطلقة ثلاثا، فإن الطلاقات الثلاث قاطعة لوصلة النكاح، ولها النفقة اتفاقاً؛ لقوله تعالى: وَإِنْ كُنَّ أُولاتِ حَمْلٍ الآية، كذا قيل. على المعتدة إلخ معطوف على قوله : على الحامل إلخ. بجامع الاحتباس متعلق بالقياس، يعني أن العلة المشتركة هو الاحتباس، والنفقة جزاء الاحتباس، فكما أن للحامل المبتوتة للمعتدة طلاق نفقة وسكنى رجعي كذلك للمطلقة ثلاثا، وقال ابن الملك: ولقائل أن يقول : انقطعت الزوجية في المبتوتة، ولا يجب لها النفقة، وليس طلاق رجعي، فلا يصح القياس. وقيل : القائل أبو جعفر الطحاوي. هو بنفسه وهو قوله: فإني سمعت إلخ. وأراد بالكتاب إلخ وقال بعضهم: أراد بالكتاب قوله تعالى: أَسْكِنُوهُنَّ مِنْ حَيْثُ سَكَنْتُمْ إلخ. ولا تخرجوهن من بيوتهن: أي مساكنهن وقت الفراق حتى يمضي عدّتهن كذا قال البيضاوي. وللمطلقات متاع بالمعروف قال قوم: المراد بالمتاع نفقة العدة، والنفقة قد تسمى متاعًا، كذا قال الحلبي في حاشية تفسير البيضاوي. يجوز العمل إلخ وجه جواز العمل أن كان في الصدر الأول فالعدالة ثابتة له باعتبار الظاهر لغلبة العدالة في ذلك الزمان، ووجه عدم وجوب العمل به أن الوجوب شرعًا لا يثبت بمثل هذا الطريق الضعيف كذا ذكر شمس الأئمة ، وأما رواية مثل هذا المجهول في زماننا فلا يقبل ولا يصح العمل بخبره ما لم يتأيد بقبول العدول لغلبة الفسق في هذا الزمان.
If nothing appears from the predecessors except rejection, it is deemed objectionable and not accepted, and this is the fourth category of the unknown narrator. Its example is what Fatima bint Qays narrated: that her husband divorced her three times, and the Messenger of Allah did not give her lodging or maintenance, and Umar rejected it, saying: 'We will not abandon the Book of our Lord and the Sunnah of our Prophet for the statement of a woman; we do not know whether she is truthful or lying, whether she remembered or forgot. Indeed, I heard the Messenger of Allah say: She deserves maintenance and lodging.' And Umar said this in the presence of the Companions, and no one objected, so there was consensus that the hadith is objectionable. But it is said: Umar intended the Book and Sunnah and analogy to the divorced pregnant woman and the woman undergoing iddah from a revocable divorce on the basis of confinement. And it is said: He himself narrated the Sunnah and intended by the Book the verse: 'Do not turn them out of their houses' regarding lodging, and 'For divorced women is provision according to what is reasonable' regarding maintenance. And if it does not appear [i.e., the hadith of the narrator], this is the fifth category of the unknown narrator: that if his hadith does not appear among the predecessors, and neither rejection nor acceptance is known, it is permissible to act upon it. No one objected, so no one accepted Fatima's hadith except a small group including Ibn Abbas, and the majority have the status of all. But it is said: The proponent [of this view] is Isa ibn Aban. He said: Umar intended [this]: that correct analogy is established by the Book and Sunnah; the Book and Sunnah are the cause of its establishment, so the cause was mentioned and the effect meant. Umar intended... on the basis that analogy is also established by the Book and Sunnah: as for the Book, His exalted saying: 'So take warning, O people of insight'; as for the hadith, it is well-known: that when the Prophet sent Muadh to Yemen as a judge, he said: 'By what will you judge?' He said: 'By the Book of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'By the Sunnah of the Messenger of Allah.' He said: 'If you do not find?' He said: 'I will exert my opinion.' So the Prophet approved him and said: 'Praise be to Allah who guided the messenger of His Messenger to what pleases Allah and His Messenger.' For the pregnant woman divorced irrevocably (al-batt): it means the woman divorced three times, for the three divorces cut the marriage bond, and she is entitled to maintenance by consensus, due to His saying: 'And if they are pregnant' etc. For the woman undergoing iddah from a revocable divorce... The shared cause is confinement, and maintenance is compensation for confinement. So just as the pregnant woman irrevocably divorced and the woman undergoing iddah from a revocable divorce have maintenance and lodging, so too the woman divorced three times. Ibn al-Malik said: It may be said: The marital bond is severed in the irrevocably divorced woman, and she is not entitled to maintenance, and it is not a revocable divorce, so the analogy is not valid. And it is said: The proponent is Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi. He himself [narrated] his saying: 'Indeed I heard' etc. And he intended by the Book etc. Some said: He intended by the Book His saying: 'House them where you reside' etc. 'And do not turn them out of their houses': i.e., their dwellings at the time of separation until their iddah expires, as al-Baydawi said. 'And for divorced women is provision according to what is reasonable': Some said 'provision' means the maintenance during iddah, and maintenance may be called provision, as al-Halabi said in his gloss on Tafsir al-Baydawi. The justification for acting upon it is that if it was in the early period, then the narrator's probity is established by outward appearance due to the prevalence of probity at that time. The reason it is not obligatory to act upon it is that obligation is not established in Islamic law by such a weak path, as Shams al-A'imma mentioned. And as for the narration of such an unknown narrator in our time, it is not accepted, and acting upon his report is not valid unless it is supported by the acceptance of reliable narrators, due to the prevalence of sinfulness in this time.
Source pages p. 516

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah, specifically the conditions of narrators. The author defines two categories of unknown (majhul) narrators. The fourth type: if the Salaf (early scholars) unanimously reject a narrator's hadith, it is deemed objectionable (mustankar) and not accepted. The example given is the hadith of Fatima bint Qays, who claimed that after a triple divorce, the Prophet did not give her lodging or maintenance. Umar ibn al-Khattab rejected this, citing the Quran (withholding of the divorced women and providing maintenance) and his own hearing from the Prophet. Since no Companion objected, this consensus showed the hadith was objectionable. However, some later scholars (like Isa ibn Aban and Abu Ja'far al-Tahawi) defended Umar's action, arguing that Umar was actually using the Quran and analogy, not rejecting the hadith outright. They said the analogy for maintenance for the pregnant divorced woman and the iddah-bound woman (from revocable divorce) was based on the illah of confinement. The fifth type: if the narrator's hadith does not appear among the Salaf at all (neither acceptance nor rejection), it is permissible to act upon it, because in the early period the default was probity. But in later times, due to prevalent sinfulness, such a report is not accepted without corroboration from reliable narrators. This passage contrasts the two categories and shows the evolution in hadith criticism within the Hanafi school.

Key Terms
المستنكر (al-mustankar): A hadith that is rejected due to being contrary to stronger evidence; here, specifically a hadith unanimously rejected by the Salaf.
المجهول (al-majhūl): An unknown narrator, one whose reliability and probity are not known from the Salaf.
الاحتباس (al-iḥtibās): Confinement (of the woman in her house during iddah) as the common cause (illah) for entitlement to maintenance.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What makes a hadith mustankar (fourth category) according to the passage?
A) The narrator is unknown and the hadith is weak.
B) The Salaf unanimously rejected the hadith.
C) The hadith contradicts the Quran.
D) The hadith is only narrated by one person.

Key Takeaway
A hadith rejected by the entire Salaf is mustankar and cannot be used as evidence; the Hanafi school follows the stronger evidence (Quran and Umar's report) for maintenance of the thrice-divorced woman.

Al-Ijma — Consensus

7 min
The Fifth Category of Majhul: Uncontested Unknown Narrators and Temporal Ruling
Defines fifth category and temporal rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the fifth category of majhul, explain its temporal ruling (acceptance in early times vs rejection in later times), and apply the distinction to a scenario.

Core Idea
An unknown narrator whose hadith neither accepted nor rejected by the Salaf may be acted upon in early times but not today without corroboration.

Not all unknown narrators are rejected. The fifth category is the 'uncontested unknown'—a narrator whose hadith did not appear among the Salaf at all, so there is no reaction. In the early Islamic period, such narrations were permissible to act upon because probity was assumed. However, in later times, due to prevalence of sinfulness, such a report is not accepted unless supported by reliable narrators. This lesson explores the logic behind this temporal shift and its implications for hadith criticism.

Guided Path
1
Define the fifth category
The fifth category is the narrator whose hadith does not appear among the Salaf, so there is neither acceptance nor rejection. Such a narrator is called 'unknown' (majhul) but not objectionable.
This is distinct from mustankar because the Salaf did not comment.
2
Understand the temporal rule
In the early period (sadr al-awwal), acting on such a narration is permissible because probity was generally assumed. The default was trustworthiness.
This is based on the zahir al-hal (outward appearance) at that time.
3
Identify the change in later times
In later times (after the early period), due to the prevalence of sinfulness (ghalabat al-fisq), such a report is not accepted unless corroborated by reliable narrators.
The default shifts from trustworthiness to suspicion.
4
Note the justification
The justification for not accepting in later times is that obligation (wujub) cannot be established by a weak path (tariq daif).
Weakness here refers to the narrator's unknown status combined with the corrupt era.
5
Apply to a scenario
If a modern narrator is unknown and no early scholar mentioned him, his hadith is rejected unless reputable scholars have accepted it.
Today, 'acceptance by reliable narrators' might mean being mentioned in authentic hadith collections or by recognized critics.

Commentary
This passage is from the chapter on the divisions of the Sunnah, specifically the conditions of narrators. The author defines two categories of unknown (majhul) narrators. Key Terms
المجهول (al-majhūl): An unknown narrator, one whose reliability and probity are not known from the Salaf.
الصدر الأول (al-sadr al-awwal): The early period of Islam (first three generations), where probity was prevalently assumed.
غلبة الفسق (ghalabat al-fisq): Prevalence of sinfulness, used to justify the stricter standard for accepting unknown narrators in later times.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is a fifth-category unknown narrator's hadith not accepted in later times without corroboration?
A) Because the Salaf rejected it.
B) Because the narrator is likely to be unreliable.
C) Because of the prevalence of sinfulness in later times.
D) Because the hadith contradicts the Quran.

Key Takeaway
The fifth category of majhul is accepted only in the early period by default; in later times, corroboration by reliable narrators is required.

Conditions for Accepting Khabar Wahid in Imposition Cases
Explains acceptance of khabar wahid in impositions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the seven conditions for accepting khabar wahid in pure imposition cases and apply them to determine the validity of testimony in financial disputes.

Core Idea
Testimony in financial impositions requires seven conditions: intellect, uprightness, precision, Islam, two witnesses, wording 'ashhadu', and freedom.

This passage from Noor al-Anwar delineates the precise conditions under which a single report (khabar wahid) is accepted as evidence in court when it imposes a liability on the defendant. The author explains that although such acceptance is based on a Quranic textual proof, it operates contrary to analogy (qiyas). Understanding these conditions is crucial for usul al-fiqh, as it illustrates how textual authority and legal reasoning combine to produce a valid evidentiary ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core ruling
State that khabar wahid is accepted in financial impositions (e.g., debts, sold items) provided certain conditions are met.
2
Recognize the textual basis and its exceptional status
Note the Quranic proof (Quran 4:15) and that this ruling is contrary to qiyas (analogy), meaning it is an exception granted by textual evidence.
The verse originally deals with witnessing against women, but is extended to financial cases by analogy of the underlying rationale.
3
List the four general conditions for reports
Identify the four conditions common to all reports: intellect (ʿaql), uprightness (ʿadālah), precision (ḍabṭ), and Islam (islām).
These are the standard conditions for accepting any khabar wahid in legal matters.
4
List the three specific conditions for imposition cases
Identify the three additional conditions: number (two witnesses), wording (the witness must say 'ashhadu'), and authority (al-walāyah, i.e., the witness must be free).
The authority condition (walāyah) is fulfilled by freedom; a slave lacks the legal capacity to impose liability through testimony.
5
Recognize the cumulative nature
Understand that all seven conditions must be present for the khabar wahid to be accepted in a pure imposition case.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وأما إثباتها بالبينات عند القاضي فيجوز بالنص على خلاف القياس، وهو قوله تعالى: فَاسْتَشْهِدُوا عَلَيْهِنَّ أَرْبَعَةً مِنْكُمْ وأمثاله، ولأن الحدود لم تثبت بالبينات، وإنما تثبت أسبابها، والحدود ثابتة بالكتاب. وإن كان من حقوق العباد مما فيه إلزام محض كخبر إثبات الحق على أحد في الديون والأعيان المبيعة والمرتمنة والمغصوبة. تشترط فيه سائر شرائط الأخبار من العقل، والعدالة، والضبط، والإسلام. مع العدد ولفظ الشهادة والولاية بأن يكون اثنين، ويتلفظ بقوله: "أشهد"، وتكون له الولاية بالحرية، فإذا اجتمعت هذه الشرائط الثلاثة مع الأربعة المتقدمة فحينئذٍ يُقبل خبر الواحد عند القاضي في المعاملات التي فيها إلزام على المدعى عليه.
As for proving them by evidences before the judge, it is permitted by textual proof contrary to analogy, and that is His statement: 'Then call to witness four witnesses from among you' and the like. And because penal punishments are not established by evidences, rather their causes are established, and the punishments are established by the Book. And if it is from the rights of people in which there is pure imposition, like report of establishing a right against someone concerning debts, sold items, pledged items, and usurped items. All the conditions of reports are required in it: intellect, uprightness, precision, and Islam. Along with number, the wording of testimony, and authority: that they be two, and he says the word 'I testify', and he has authority by freedom. So when these three conditions are combined with the four preceding ones, then the single report is accepted before the judge in transactions in which there is imposition on the defendant.
Source pages p. 534

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the conditions for accepting a single report (khabar wahid) as evidence in court when it imposes a liability on the defendant. The author explains that proving such rights by witnesses is allowed by textual proof (Quranic verse on witnessing against women) even though it is contrary to analogy (qiyas) because penalties are not proven by witnesses but by explicit texts. However, in financial rights with pure imposition, full conditions are required: intelligence, uprightness, precision, Islam, two witnesses, the word 'ashhadu', and freedom (walaayah). When these conditions are met, the report is accepted in transactional matters where the defendant is bound.

Key Terms
البينة (al-bayyinah): Evidence, specifically testimony of witnesses that establishes a right in court.
الولاية (al-walāyah): Authority, meaning the witness must have legal capacity to enforce testimony, i.e., must be free.
الإلزام (al-ilzām): Imposition, meaning the testimony creates a binding obligation on the defendant.

B) Seven conditions: the four plus number, wording of testimony, and freedom.
C) Three conditions: number, wording, and authority.
D) Two conditions: testimony and freedom.

Key Takeaway
Khabar wahid in financial imposition cases is accepted only when seven conditions are met: four general (intellect, uprightness, precision, Islam) and three specific (two witnesses, wording 'ashhadu', and freedom).

Narrator Denial and Rejection of Hadith
Rule on narrator denial impact

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule for rejecting a hadith when the narrator denies or forgets, and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
A narrator's forgetfulness voids his narration in Hanafi usul, unlike Shafi'i.

This passage from a Hanafi usul work discusses when a hadith is invalidated because the narrator (the one from whom it is transmitted) denies or forgets. The core distinction is between categorical denial (unanimous rejection) and hesitant denial (disputed). This lesson unpacks the Hanafi position and its proof.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of denial
Recognize the terms إنكار جاحد (categorical denial) and إنكار متوقف (hesitant denial). In categorical denial, the narrator flatly says 'You lied against me, I never narrated this.' In hesitant denial, he says 'I do not remember' or 'I do not know.'
The type of denial determines the ruling.
2
State the ruling for each type
For categorical denial, the hadith is dropped by consensus (ittifaq). For hesitant denial, the Hanafi school (al-Karkhi, Abu Yusuf, Ahmad ibn Hanbal) holds it is dropped; the Shafi'i and Maliki schools say it is not dropped.
The ikhtilaf is only for hesitant denial.
3
Examine the Hanafi proof
The Hanafi argument: Forgetfulness indicates heedlessness (mughaffal). The narration of a heedless person is not accepted. Since the origin (the narrator's denial) and the branch (the transmitted report) contradict each other, one must be false, casting doubt.
This is a logical talil (reasoning).
4
Analyze the opposing school proof
Shafi'i and Malik argue: Both narrators are trustworthy (adi). A person may narrate something and later truly forget. Forgetfulness does not invalidate the initial reliability. The presumption of truth remains.
They prioritize the original transmission over later forgetfulness.
5
Apply the rule to the example
The example of Ibn Jurayj and al-Zuhri: Ibn Jurayj narrated a hadith from al-Zuhri about marriage without guardian. When asked, al-Zuhri said 'I do not know it' and suggested the sub-narrator made a mistake. Under Hanafi rule, the hadith is dropped because al-Zuhri's hesitant denial indicates forgetfulness.
This hadith is accepted by Shafi'is but rejected by Hanafis.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان طعن يلحق الحديث] ولما فرغ عن بيان التقسيمات الأربع شرع في بيان طعن يلحق الحديث من جانب أي مما يختص بالسنن الراوي أو من غيره، فقال: بيان طعن يلحق الحديث] والمروي عنه إذا أنكر الرواية، فإن كان إنكار جاحد بأن يقول: "كذبت علي، وما رويتُ لك هذا يسقط العمل بالحديث ،اتفاقًا، وإن كان إنكار متوقف بأن قال: "لا أذكر أني رويتُ لك هذا الحديث" أو "لا أعرفه" ففيه خلاف، فعند الكر خي عليه وأحمد وأبي يوسف به بن حنبل له يسقط العمل به وعند الشافعي ومالك لا يسقط. ومحمد الله أو عَمِل بخلافه بعد الرواية مما هو خلاف بيقين سقط العمل به؛ لأنه إن خالفه للوقوف إنكار جاحد إلخ مثاله ما روى ابن جُريج عن سليمان بن موسى عن الزهري عن عروة، عن عائشة لها أن رسول الله ل الله قال: "أيما امرأة نكحت بغير إذن وليها فنكاحها "باطل" كذا في "جامع الترمذي"، قال ابن عدي في "الكامل": قال ابن جريج: لقيت الزهري وسألته عن هذا الحديث فقال: "لا أعرفه" فقلت: أخبرنا أنك حدثته بهذا، فأثنى الزهري على سليمان ابن موسى وقال: أخشى أنه وهم علي. كذا في سلیمان بن موسى كذب "فتح القدير". (القمر) يسقط العمل إلخ لأن كل واحد من الأصل والفرع مُكَذِّب للآخر، فلا بد من واحد، فلزم القدح في الحديث (القمر) إنكار متوقف إلخ : مثاله أنه قال عبد العزيز بن محمد الدراوردي سهلًا: إنه حدثني ربيعة منك أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قضى بشاهد ويمين؟ فلم يتذكر سهل. كذا قيل. (القمر) يسقط العمل به لأن المروي عنه إذا لم يتذكّر بالتذكير كان مُغفّلاً، ورواية المغفّل لا تقبل إلا أن الراوي والمروي عنه باقيان على عدالتهما، فلو رويا حديثا آخر يقبل لبقاء احتمال الخطأ والنسيان. (القمر) لا يسقط لأن كل واحد من الراوي والمروي عنه عدل ،ثقة والإنسان قد يروي شيئاً لغيره ثم ينسى بعد مدةٍ، فلا يبطل ما ترجّح من جهة الصدق بعدالته بالنسيان (القمر) بخلافه أي بخلاف الحديث الذي رواه ذلك المروي عنه. (القمر) مما هو إلخ: أي من جنس ما هو بخلاف بيقين، أي لا يحتمل أن يكون مرادا من الخبر. Explanation of a criticism that affects the hadith. When he finished the explanation of the four divisions, he began to explain a criticism that affects the hadith from the side of the narrator or from others. He said: Explanation of a criticism that affects the hadith. If the one narrated from denies the narration—if it is a denial of rejection such that he says, 'You lied against me, I did not narrate this to you'—then acting upon the hadith is dropped by consensus. If it is a hesitant denial such that he says, 'I do not remember that I narrated this hadith to you' or 'I do not know it,' then there is disagreement. According to al-Karkhi, Ahmad, and Abu Yusuf, acting upon it is dropped; according to al-Shafi'i and Malik, it is not dropped. And Muhammad. Or if he acts contrary to it after narrating it, in a way that is definitely contrary, then acting upon it is dropped. Because he contradicted it— Examples of categorical denial: Ibn Jurayj narrated from Sulayman ibn Musa from al-Zuhri from Urwa from Aisha that the Messenger of God said: 'Any woman who marries without her guardian's permission, her marriage is invalid.' Quoted in Jami' al-Tirmidhi. Ibn Adi in al-Kamil said: Ibn Jurayj said: I met al-Zuhri and asked him about this hadith, and he said: 'I do not know it.' I said: 'He informed us that you narrated it to him.' Then al-Zuhri praised Sulayman ibn Musa and said: 'I fear he made a mistake about me.' Quoted in Fath al-Qadir. (al-Qamar) 'Acting upon it is dropped etc.' Because each of the origin and the branch accuses the other of lying, so one must prevail, so the hadith is impugned. (al-Qamar) 'Hesitant denial etc.' Example: Abd al-Aziz ibn Muhammad al-Darawirdi said to Sahl: 'He narrated to me from Rabi'a from you that the Prophet judged by a witness and an oath?' Sahl did not remember. So it is said. (al-Qamar) 'Acting upon it is dropped' because if the one narrated from does not remember when reminded, he is heedless (mughaffal), and the narration of a heedful person is not accepted. (al-Qamar) 'It is not dropped' because each of the narrator and the one narrated from is just and trustworthy, and a person may narrate something to another and then forget after a time, so what is deemed trustworthy by their justice is not invalidated by forgetfulness. (al-Qamar) 'contrary to it' i.e., contrary to the hadith that the narrator narrated. (al-Qamar) 'That which is etc.' i.e., of the same type as something definitely contrary, i.e., it is not possible that it was meant by the report. (al-Qamar) 'Acting upon it is dropped'—As for acting contrary to the apparent meaning of the hadith, like if the hadith is absolute and the Companion acted upon a restriction, or general and the Companion specified it, then acting upon the apparent is prevented; rather, it is interpreted in a way consistent with the Companion's action. The just Companion does not act contrary to the apparent because acting contrary to the apparent is forbidden; no sensible person would dare, unless he has an observed contextual clue that causes the hadith to be diverted from the apparent. Otherwise, his justice would be impaired. As for the non- Companion narrator acting contrary to the apparent, it does not necessitate abandoning the apparent, for he does not observe contextual clues, and there is no verbal clue in the statement.
Source pages p. 545

Commentary
This passage discusses factors that invalidate a hadith based on the narrator's own statements or actions. It is a commentary from a Hanafi usul work. The author explains that if the person from whom the hadith is transmitted (al-marwi 'anhu) denies narrating it altogether (e.g., 'You lied, I never told you that'), then the hadith is unanimously rejected. If he expresses doubt ('I don't remember' or 'I don't know'), there is disagreement: Hanafi scholars like al-Karkhi, Abu Yusuf, and Ahmad ibn Hanbal say the hadith is rejected because the narrator's forgetfulness implies heedlessness (mughaffal), while al-Shafi'i and Malik say it is not rejected because forgetfulness does not negate the initial reliability. The text provides an example: Ibn Jurayj narrated a hadith from al-Zuhri, who later denied knowing it; al-Zuhri suggested the sub-narrator might have made a mistake. The commentary sides with those who drop the hadith in such cases, using logical reasoning that one of the two must be mistaken. Additionally, if a narrator acts contrary to his own hadith in a definitively contradictory manner, the hadith is rejected. This is because his action shows he does not consider it binding, and his integrity is questioned. However, if a Companion acts contrary to the apparent meaning of a hadith (e.g., restricting an absolute text), that does not necessarily reject the hadith; it may indicate a contextual clue known only to him. Non- Companion narrators' contrary actions do not affect the hadith's validity since they lack such contextual knowledge.

Key Terms
إنكار جاحد (inkār jāḥid): A denial where the narrator explicitly accuses the transmitter of lying and says he never narrated it.
إنكار متوقف (inkār mutawaqqif): A hesitant denial where the narrator says he does not remember or does not know the hadith.
المغفل (al-mughaffal): A person who is heedless or forgetful, whose narration is not accepted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) The hadith is still accepted
B) The hadith is rejected because of forgetfulness
C) The hadith is rejected only if the narrator is known to lie
D) The hadith is accepted if another narrator confirms it

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rejects a hadith if the narrator denies it, either categorically (unanimous) or hesitantly (due to forgetfulness), while the Shafi'i school only rejects categorical denial.

Bayan Darurah: Clarification through Silence
Explains how the Lawgiver's silence serves as clarification (bayan) due to necessity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify when silence constitutes a binding form of bayan (clarification) and apply the Hanafi rule that silence, under specific conditions, indicates permissibility or tacit approval.

Core Idea
Silence, when observed with the ability to object, speaks louder than words — it becomes a binding legal clarification.

In Hanafi usul, clarification (bayan) is not limited to explicit statements; it can also be established through the implication of the speaker's state (dalalat al-hal). This lesson explores one of the most powerful forms of contextual clarification: bayan darurah (clarification by necessity), where silence under certain conditions is interpreted as a definitive legal indication. We will examine how the lawgiver's silence—or the silence of any qualified authority—can convey permissibility, and how the necessity of preventing deception (gharar) justifies treating silence as permission in transactions.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of bayan darurah
Grasp that bayan darurah is a form of contextual clarification where the speaker's silence, in a situation where objection is possible, is treated as a clear indication of permissibility or consent.
The 'speaker' here is the person who could object; the silence is interpreted by the state (hal).
2
Identify the conditions for legally binding silence
Note the two conditions: (1) The observer must have the ability to object (qudra ala al-inkar). (2) The actor must be Muslim. If these are met, silence indicates permissibility.
The passage explicitly states: 'بشرط القدرة على الإنكار، وكون الفاعل مسلما'.
3
Analyze the first example: silence of the Lawgiver and Companions
The Prophet's silence when seeing an action without disapproving is considered a command of permissibility. Similarly, the Companions' silence in the incident of the slave woman before 'Umar constituted a consensus (ijma) that benefits are not compensable.
The 'Umar incident involved a runaway slave woman; the Companions did not object to 'Umar's silence regarding compensation for benefits.
4
Examine the debated case: master's silence as permission for the slave to trade
When a master sees his slave engaging in trade and remains silent, the Hanafi school treats this as permission (idhn) based on the necessity of preventing deception to third parties. Imam Zufar disagreed, citing ambiguity.
The Hanafi response invokes custom ('urf): a disapproving master would normally forbid and discipline.
5
Recognize the role of darurah and 'urf in weighing probabilities
Silence is inherently probable (zanni), but the necessity of avoiding gharar and the prevalence of custom (urf) give it suficent weight to be considered a binding proof.
This exemplifies the Hanafi reliance on istihsan and 'urf in usul.

Source Text

بدلالة حال المتكلم : أي حال المتكلّم يدل على أن السكوت بسبب رضاه، ولما كان يرد عليه أن الساكت ساكت فلِمَ عبر عنه بالمتكلم؟ أجاب عنه الشارح بقوله: أي حال إلخ: يعني أن المراد أن الساكت متكلم بلسان الحال إلا بلسان المقال، فكأنه متكلم بلسان المقال، ولذا عبّر عنه بالمتكلّم (القمر) أي حال الساكت إلخ: هذا دفع دخل مقدر، وهو أن صاحب الحال لما كان متكلما فما الحاجة إلى إثبات الحكم بدلالة الحال؛ لأن الكلام موجود، فينبغي أن يثبت به وأيضًا لا يصح مثاله بسكوت صاحب الشرع؛ لأن سكوته يستلزم أن لا يكون متكلما، فلا يطابق المثال للممثل له؟ وتقرير الدفع: أن المراد بالمتكلم متكلم بلسان الحال لا بلسان القال فلا منافاة، ويصح حينئذ إثبات الحكم بدلالة الحال. (السنبلي) صاحب الشرع: أي النبي وأصحابه . (القمر) كالمضاربات والشركات المضاربة عقد شركة في الربح بمال من جانب وعمل من جانب، والشركة عبارة عن عقد بين المتشاركين في الأصل والربح، كذا في "الدر المختار". بالإتلاف أو ثبت ضرورة دفع الغرور عن الناس، وهو حرام كسكوت المولى حين رأى
أي الغرور
عبده يبيع ويشتري فإنه يصير إذنًا له في التجارة عندنا؛ لأنه لو لم يكن مأذونا يتضرّر الناس به، ودفع الغرور عنهم واجب، وقال زفر له لا يكون مأذونا؛ لأن سكوته
المولى
يحتمل أن يكون للرضا بتصرفه وأن يكون لفرط الغيظ ، والمحتمل لا يكون حجة. أو ثبت ضرورة كثرة الكلام أي كثرة استعماله أو طول عبارته يدل على ما هو المراد
فكان إجماعا إلخ وسند الإجماع أن المنافع مطلقة ليس بمتقومة؛ لأنها ليست بمال؛ لأن المال ما يمكن إحرازه والمنافع لا تبقى زمانين فلا تكون مضمونة (السنبلي) فكان إجماعًا لأن المولى جاء طالبا لحقه، وهو حاصل بما يجب له، وهذه حادثة وقعت بعد رسول الله ، ولم يسمع فيها نص فكان الواجب على الصحابة له البيان بصفة الكمال، فلما سكتوا عن بيان قيمة المنفعة صار هذا دليل النفي لا يقال: إنما سكتوا عن بيان قيمة المنفعة لكون الولد صغيرًا، فلم يكن له منفعة؛ لأنا نقول قد ثبت في الروايات كلها أنهم سكتوا عن تقويم منافعه، فدلّ على أن المنافع كانت موجودة وأن الولد كان كبيرًا، كذا في "التحقيق". (القمر) ولد المغرور إلخ من يطأ امرأة
بالقيمة.(القمر)
معتمدًا على ملك اليمين أو على النكاح ظانا أنها حرّة، فتلد منه ثم تستحق وولده هذا حرّ بالقيمة. (القمر) أو ثبت ضرورة إلخ يعني أنه لو لم يحصل هذا البيان لزم الغرور ، وهو حرام فدفعه ضروري لازم في الدين، فلضرورة دفع الغرور قيل بهذا البيان. (القمر) فإنه يصير إلخ أي فإن هذا السكوت يصير إذنًا للعبد في التجارة في عقد يباشر العبد بعد هذا السكوت لا في عقد وقع السكوت فيه؛ لأن السكوت الذي هو بيان يتحقق بعد هذا العقد، فهذا العقد قبل السكوت وجد بلا دليل كذا قال أعظم العلماء مولانا عبد السلام الأعظمي . (القمر) يتضرّر الناس به إلخ فإن الناس يعاملونه بالبيع والشراء اعتمادًا على سكوت المولى، فإذا لحقه ديون فيقول المولى إنه محجور ما أذنته للتجارة، فتتأخر الديون إلى وقت عتقه، ففيه ضرر لأصحاب الديون وغررهم، فلابد أن يجعل سكوته إذنًا دفعًا لهذا الغرور (القمر) لا يكون حجة ونحن نقول: إن السكوت وإن كان محتملا لكن العرف مرجّح، فإن العادة جارية بأن من لا يرضى بتصرّف عبده يصرّح بالنهي إذا رآه يتصرف، بل يؤدبه على ذالك (القمر) أي كثرة استعماله إلخ نبه بهذا التفسير على أن لكلام المصنف الله محملين: الأول: أن كثرة الكلام أي كثرة استعمال البيان يدلّ على ما هو المراد؛ فلا حاجة إلى ما ذكره، فيثبت البيان ضرورة كثرة استعماله والثاني: أن كثرة الكلام أي طول عبارة الكلام لو ذكر البيان كان باعثا على عدم ذكره، والقرينة قائمة على ثبوت البيان المسكوت عنه فيثبت البيان. (القمر)
Section on the divisions of clarification. Clarification by necessity: or it is established by the implication of the state of the speaker, i.e., the state of the silent person who is speaking with the tongue of state, not with the tongue of speech, like the silence of the Lawgiver when he observes an affair without changing it. That is, when the Messenger (peace be upon him) saw a matter—any statement or action related to silence—that they [the companions] performed and dealt with, such as partnerships and companies, or saw something being sold in the market and did not disapprove of it, he knew it was permissible. So his silence is placed in the position of a command of permissibility. The same ruling applies to the silence of the Companions, provided there is ability to object and that the doer is Muslim. As narrated that a slave woman ran away and married a man, then gave birth to children from Banu 'Udhrah or children, then her master came and raised the case to 'Umar. He ruled the slave woman for her master and ruled against the father (i.e., the slave woman) that he should ransom the children and take them by payment of their value, and he remained silent about guaranteeing her benefits and the benefits of her children, from intercourse and service. By the implication of the state of the speaker: the state of the speaker indicates that his silence is due to his consent. And since it could be objected that the silent person is silent, why is he called a speaker? The commentator answered with his statement: 'i.e., the state etc.': meaning that the intent is that the silent person is speaking with the tongue of state, not with the tongue of speech, so he is as if he were speaking with the tongue of speech, and therefore he is called a speaker. (al-Qamar) 'i.e., the state of the silent etc.': This is a refutation of an anticipated objection: since the owner of the state is a speaker, what need is there to establish the ruling by the implication of the state? Because speech exists, so it should be established by it. Also, the example with the silence of the Lawgiver is not valid because his silence entails that he is not a speaker, so the example does not match what is being exemplified. The explanation of the refutation: the intended meaning of 'speaker' is a speaker with the tongue of state, not with the tongue of speech, so there is no contradiction, and it is then valid to establish the ruling by the implication of the state. (al-Sunbuli) 'Lawgiver': i.e., the Prophet and his Companions. (al-Qamar) 'like partnerships and companies': Mudaraba is a contract of partnership in profit with capital from one side and work from the other; company is a contract between partners in capital and profit, as in al-Durr al-Mukhtar. (al-Qamar) 'so his silence is placed etc.': i.e., provided that there is no statement from the Messenger prior to this silence indicating that it is forbidden, for then the silence does not indicate permissibility. Thus it is said. But it is also said: the silence in that case also indicates permissibility, for it abrogates the previous statement indicating prohibition, since if the prohibition were not abrogated, the silence would be an abandonment of duty, i.e., informing of the forbidden, and that is far from the station of the Prophet. (al-Qamar) 'and that the doer etc.': co-ordinated with 'ability', i.e., provided the doer is Muslim. So the silence of the Lawgiver when a disbeliever eats pork does not indicate its permissibility, nor when he abandons prayer. (al-Qamar) 'he ruled with it etc.': i.e., with the slave woman. (al-Qamar) 'and takes them by payment of their value': and they become free. (al-Qamar) 'this wording': but Razin narrated from Malik and mentioned in the Muwatta' that it reached him that 'Umar or 'Uthman ruled in a case of a slave woman who deceived a man pretending to be free and bore him children; he ruled that the father should ransom his children with similar slaves. Malik said: 'Payment of their value is more just, God willing.' [Ishraq al-Absar: 25] Rare from... Section on the divisions of clarification: and that was in the presence of the Companions, and so it was a consensus that the benefits of the child of the deceived are not guaranteed. Or it is established by the necessity of removing deception (gharar) from the people, and that is prohibited. Like the silence of the master when he sees his slave buying and selling: then it becomes permission (idhn) for him to trade according to us, because if he were not permitted, people would suffer harm, and removing deception from them is obligatory. Zufar said: he does not become permitted, because the master's silence could be due to consent to his action or due to extreme anger, and the probable is not proof. Or it is established by the necessity of abundant speech, i.e., frequent usage, or lengthy expression indicating what is intended. 'So it was a consensus etc.': The basis of consensus is that benefits are absolute and not compensable because they are not property; property is what can be preserved, and benefits do not endure for two moments, so they are not guaranteed. (al-Sunbuli) 'So it was a consensus': because the master came demanding his right, and it is obtained by what is due to him. This incident occurred after the Messenger of God, and no text was heard concerning it. So it was obligatory on the Companions to clarify for him perfectly. When they remained silent about clarifying the value of the benefit, this became evidence of negation. It cannot be said: they remained silent about clarifying the value of the benefit because the child was young, so he had no benefit; for we say: it is established in all the transmissions that they remained silent about evaluating its benefits, so that indicates that the benefits were present and that the child was an adult. Thus in al-Tahqiq. (al-Qamar) 'child of the deceived etc.': he who has intercourse with a woman based on ownership of the right hand or marriage, thinking she is free, and she gives birth from him, then she is reclaimed, and the child is free for a compensation. (al-Qamar) 'or established by necessity etc.': meaning if this clarification did not happen, deception would result, and that is prohibited, so its avoidance is necessary and binding in religion. So for the necessity of removing deception, this clarification was stated. (al-Qamar) 'then it becomes etc.': i.e., this silence becomes permission for the slave to trade in contracts he undertakes after this silence, not in the contract in which the silence occurred, because the silence which is clarification is realized after that contract. This contract before the silence exists without evidence. Thus said the greatest scholar, our master 'Abd al-Salam al-A'zami. (al-Qamar) 'people suffer harm etc.': people deal with him by selling and buying relying on the master's silence. If he incurs debts, the master says: he is interdicted, I did not permit him to trade, so the debts are postponed until his emancipation. That harms the creditors and deceives them. So it is necessary to make his silence permission to avoid this deception. (al-Qamar) 'is not proof': and we say: although the silence is probable, custom (urf) gives preponderance. For the customary practice is that one who does not approve of his slave's action clearly forbids when he sees him acting, even disciplines him for that. (al-Qamar) 'i.e., frequent usage etc.': This interpretation points out that the author's statement has two meanings: first, that abundant speech (i.e., frequent usage of clarification) indicates what is intended, so there is no need for what was mentioned, and clarification is established by the necessity of its frequent usage. Second, that abundant speech (i.e., lengthy expression) if clarification were mentioned would be a cause for not mentioning it, and the contextual evidence indicates the establishment of the omitted clarification, so it is established. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 588

Commentary
This passage from a Hanafi usul commentary discusses the concept of bayan darurah (clarification by necessity), focusing on how silence (sukut) can serve as a legally binding form of clarification. The author begins by stating that bayan darurah is established through the implication (dalala) of the state (hal) of the speaker—meaning that even a silent person, when his state indicates consent, is considered 'speaking' in a metaphorical sense. The primary example is the silence of the Lawgiver (the Prophet, peace be upon him) when observing an action without objection. Such silence is interpreted as a command of permissibility (ibaha). This is extended to the silence of the Companions, provided they have the ability to object and the actor is Muslim. The text then narrates a famous incident: a slave woman ran away, married a man, had children. When the master came, 'Umar (may God be pleased with him) ruled that the children be ransomed by their father for their value, but remained silent about compensation for the benefits (services and intercourse) of the slave woman and children. The Companions present were silent, which is considered a consensus (ijma) that such benefits are not compensable because they are not considered property (mal) in the sense of being preservable. The passage also addresses the case of a master seeing his slave buying and selling: according to the Hanafi school, his silence constitutes permission (idhn) for the slave to trade, based on the necessity of avoiding deception (gharar) to the public. Imam Zufar disagreed, arguing that silence is ambiguous, but the Hanafis counter by invoking 'urf (custom): the customary practice is that a displeased master would explicitly forbid and discipline. Thus, silence with the possibility of objection is interpreted as consent due to the prevalent custom. Finally, the passage mentions another type of bayan darurah: the necessity arising from abundant usage or lengthy expression, where the context itself indicates the intended meaning.

Key Terms
بيان (bayan): Clarification or manifestation of a legal ruling by a means other than explicit statement, such as silence or context.
سكوت (sukut): Silence, which under certain conditions serves as a form of bayan that indicates permissibility or tacit approval.
ضرورة (darurah): Necessity that makes a ruling or clarification imperative to avoid harm (such as gharar).
غرور (gharur): Deception or risk that leads to harm; avoiding it is a legal necessity.
إذن (idhn): Permission, particularly the master's tacit permission for the slave to engage in trade.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view presented in this passage, what is one necessary condition for the silence of the Lawgiver (or a qualified authority) to indicate permissibility?
A) The silence must occur after an explicit command of prohibition.
B) The actor must be a Muslim.
C) The silence must be accompanied by a verbal statement of approval.
D) The action must be related to trade and commerce.

Key Takeaway
Silence, when observed with the ability to object, serves as a binding form of clarification (bayan darurah) indicating permissibility or tacit approval, provided the actor is Muslim and necessity or custom supports the interpretation.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
8 min
Necessity and 'Urf in Hanafi Usul: The Master's Silence
Commentary on necessity-based clarification with ijma and 'urf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule that silence becomes permission when supported by 'urf and necessity, and evaluate Zufar's objection that silence is ambiguous.

Core Idea
Necessity and custom transform ambiguous silence into legal permission to prevent deception.

When no explicit text exists, Hanafi usul allows deriving rulings from necessity, consensus (ijma), and custom ('urf). This lesson explores a classic case: the master's silence when seeing his slave trade. The Hanafis treat this silence as implicit permission, while Zufar rejects it as ambiguous. We will dissect the proofs, including an ijma from the Companions, and see how 'urf tips the scale.

Guided Path
1
Identify the issue and the two positions
State the legal question: Does a master's silence when seeing his slave engage in trade constitute permission? Note the Hanafi position (yes) and Zufar's (no).
2
Understand the ijma proof from the child of al-maghrur
The Companions, after the Prophet's time, faced a case: a child born from a deceived marriage. They ruled that the child's benefits (manafi') are not guaranteed. Their silence about evaluating these benefits became ijma that manafi' are not valuable property. This shows how necessity and silence can create a proof.
The incident is used as a parallel to the master's silence case.
3
Analyze Zufar's objection
Zufar argues that silence is ambiguous—it could be consent or anger—so it cannot serve as a proof (hujja). Understand the basis of his objection: probability is not certainty.
4
Examine the Hanafi response using 'urf
Hanafis concede that silence is ambiguous in itself, but custom ('urf) clarifies it: a master who disapproves will explicitly forbid and discipline. Thus, silence indicates consent. Necessity also plays a role: without permission, creditors are harmed.
This is an example of 'urf as a tarjih (preferentiator) in usul.
5
Extract the broader principle of bayan al-darura
The passage also discusses how frequency of usage (kathrat al-istimal) or length of expression can serve as a contextual indicator (qarina) to establish a clarification. This is part of the category 'bayan al-darura'—clarification by necessity.
All examples show that necessity, consensus, and custom are subsidiary sources in Hanafi usul.

فصل في أقسام البيان وكان ذلك بمحضر من الصحابة ، فكان إجماعًا على أن منافع ولد المغرور لا تضمن بالإتلاف أو ثبت ضرورة دفع الغرور عن الناس، وهو حرام كسكوت المولى حين رأى عبده يبيع ويشتري فإنه يصير إذنًا له في التجارة عندنا؛ لأنه لو لم يكن مأذونا يتضرّر الناس به، ودفع الغرور عنهم واجب، وقال زفر له لا يكون مأذونا؛ لأن سكوته يحتمل أن يكون للرضا بتصرفه وأن يكون لفرط الغيظ ، والمحتمل لا يكون حجة. أو ثبت ضرورة كثرة الكلام أي كثرة استعماله أو طول عبارته يدل على ما هو المراد فكان إجماعا إلخ وسند الإجماع أن المنافع مطلقة ليس بمتقومة؛ لأنها ليست بمال؛ لأن المال ما يمكن إحرازه والمنافع لا تبقى زمانين فلا تكون مضمونة (السنبلي) فكان إجماعًا لأن المولى جاء طالبا لحقه، وهو حاصل بما يجب له، وهذه حادثة وقعت بعد رسول الله ، ولم يسمع فيها نص فكان الواجب على الصحابة له البيان بصفة الكمال، فلما سكتوا عن بيان قيمة المنفعة صار هذا دليل النفي لا يقال: إنما سكتوا عن بيان قيمة المنفعة لكون الولد صغيرًا، فلم يكن له منفعة؛ لأنا نقول قد ثبت في الروايات كلها أنهم سكتوا عن تقويم منافعه، فدلّ على أن المنافع كانت موجودة وأن الولد كان كبيرًا، كذا في "التحقيق". (القمر) ولد المغرور إلخ من يطأ امرأة بالقيمة.(القمر) معتمدًا على ملك اليمين أو على النكاح ظانا أنها حرّة، فتلد منه ثم تستحق وولده هذا حرّ بالقيمة. (القمر)
Section on the types of bayan: And that [the incident of the child of al-maghrur] occurred in the presence of the Companions, so it was a consensus that the benefits of the child of the deceived one are not guaranteed by destruction, or [it was] established by the necessity of removing deception from people, and it is forbidden. Like the silence of the master when he saw his slave buying and selling, for it becomes permission for him to engage in trade according to us; because if he were not permitted, people would be harmed by him, and removing deception from them is obligatory. Zufar said: He does not become permitted because his silence could be for satisfaction with his action or for extreme anger, and a probable [indication] is not a proof. Or [it was] established by the necessity of frequency of speech, i.e., frequency of its usage or length of its expression indicates what is intended. "So it was a consensus, etc." The basis of the consensus is that benefits are absolute, not valuable; because they are not property, because property is what can be possessed, and benefits do not persist for two moments, so they are not guaranteed. (al-Sunbuli) "So it was a consensus" because the master came seeking his right, and it is obtained by what is due to him, and this incident occurred after the Messenger of Allah, and no text was heard regarding it, so it was obligatory upon the Companions to give a complete clarification. When they remained silent about stating the value of the benefit, this became evidence of negation. It cannot be said: They only remained silent about stating the value of the benefit because the child was young, so he had no benefit; for we say: It is established in all narrations that they remained silent about evaluating his benefits, so this indicates that benefits existed and the child was older. Thus in "al-Tahqiq". (al-Qamar) "Child of the deceived one, etc.": One who has intercourse with a woman by value, relying on ownership by right hand or marriage, thinking she is free, then she gives birth from him, then she is claimed, and this child is free with [payment of] value. (al-Qamar) "Or established by necessity, etc.": It means that if this clarification did not occur, deception would be necessary, and it is forbidden, so repelling it is necessary in the religion; for the necessity of repelling deception, this clarification was stated. (al-Qamar) "For it becomes, etc.": That is, this silence becomes permission for the slave to trade in a contract that the slave undertakes after this silence, not in a contract in which the silence occurred; because the silence which is clarification occurs after this contract, so this contract before the silence existed without evidence. Thus said the greatest scholar our master Abd al-Salam al-A'zami. (al-Qamar) "People are harmed by him, etc.": People deal with him in buying and selling relying on the silence of the master. If debts are incurred on him, the master says he is interdicted, I did not permit him to trade, so the debts are delayed until his emancipation. In this is harm to the creditors and deception for them, so his silence must be made permission to repel this deception. (al-Qamar) "Is not a proof": And we say: Even if the silence is probable, but custom (urf) is a preference; for the habit is that whoever is not satisfied with his slave's action explicitly forbids when he sees him acting,  rather he disciplines him for that. (al-Qamar) "i.e., frequency of its usage, etc.": He alerts by this interpretation that the author's statement has two possible meanings: First, that frequency of speech, i.e., frequent usage of bayan, indicates what is intended, so there is no need for what he mentioned; thus bayan is established by the necessity of its frequent usage. Second, that frequency of speech, i.e., length of expression; if he mentioned the bayan, it would be a cause for not mentioning it, and the contextual indicator (qarina) exists for the existence of the omitted bayan, so the bayan is established. (al-Qamar)
Source pages p. 589

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the types of bayan (clarification), focusing on 'bayan al-darura' (clarification by necessity). The author discusses several legal proofs: First, the incident of the child of al-maghrur, where the Companions reached consensus (ijma) that the benefits (manafi') of the child are not guaranteed when destroyed because they are not considered property (mal) in the full sense; they are temporary and cannot be hoarded. This consensus also established that necessity prevents deception (gharar). Second, the example of a master's silence when seeing his slave trade: According to the Hanafi school (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), this silence becomes implicit permission (idhn) due to custom ('urf) and to avoid harming third parties. Zufar disagrees, arguing silence is ambiguous and not proof. The Hanafi response relies on 'urf as a preponderant factor, since a master who disapproves would normally forbid and discipline. Third, the necessity of frequent usage (kathrat al-istimal) or lengthy expression to indicate the intended meaning. The commentator explains that frequency can itself serve as a qarina (contextual indicator) establishing the existence of an omitted bayan. All points illustrate how necessity, custom, and consensus are used as sources for rulings in Hanafi usul.

Key Terms
بيان الضرورة (bayan al-darura): A type of clarification necessitated by the need to remove harm or deception, even without explicit textual proof.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the Companions on a ruling when no text exists, used here as proof that manafi' are not guaranteed.
عرف (urf): Customary practice used to give preference to one interpretation of an ambiguous act (silence).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did the Hanafis consider the master's silence as permission for the slave to trade, despite Zufar's objection?
A) Because silence is always a clear proof of consent
B) Because custom ('urf) indicates that a displeased master would explicitly forbid
C) Because the slave's actions were beneficial to the master
D) Because the master had previously allowed trade verbally

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi usul, silence can become a legal proof when supported by custom and necessity, as demonstrated by the master's tacit permission for his slave's trade.
