Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
10 min
The Condition of Unanimity for Ijma'
Explains that for Ijma' all mujtahids must agree; one dissenter prevents it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi condition for valid Ijma' (agreement of all mujtahids) and explain why a single dissenter prevents it, using the hadith and the verse on Abraham.

Core Idea
For Ijma' to be binding, every mujtahid must agree; one dissenter breaks the consensus.

Ijma' is a primary source of Islamic law, but its authority depends on strict conditions. The Hanafi school holds that consensus requires the unanimous agreement of all mujtahids of an era. This lesson unpacks that condition, the proof behind it, and the scholarly debate on the minimum number needed for Ijma'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the condition for Ijma'
The passage states that the condition (shart) for Ijma' is 'ijtima' al-kull' — the gathering of all mujtahids. A single dissenter prevents the formation of consensus, just as a majority dissent would.
2
Analyze the primary proof
The proof is the hadith: 'My community will not agree on error.' The term 'community' (ummah) encompasses all mujtahids. If even one dissents, the 'whole' is not present, so consensus cannot form.
The hadith is mutawatir in meaning, giving it strong epistemological weight.
3
Examine the dispute on minimum number
Scholars differ on the minimum number of mujtahids required for Ijma'. Views include: three (al-Sarakhsi), two, or even one (based on the verse 'Indeed Abraham was an ummah'). The Hanafi chosen view considers unanimity of all, but if only one mujtahid remains, his view is considered Ijma'.
The dispute is a legitimate ikhtilaf; each view has backing.
4
Understand the implication for binding authority
If Ijma' is formed, it is binding; a dissenter's opinion is overruled. If consensus is not reached (due to dissent), the matter remains open to ijtihad. The passage also notes that subsequent consensus after prior disagreement is considered weak (like khabar al-wahid) and does not lead to takfir of deniers.
This affects the force of Ijma' in legal practice.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان شرط الإجماع
والشرط اجتماع الكل، وخلاف الواحد مانع كخلاف الأكثر، يعني في حين انعقاد عن الإجماع الإجماع لو خالف واحد كان خلافه معتبرًا ولا ينعقد الإجماع؛ لأن لفظ الأمة في قوله علي: "لا تجتمع أمني على الضلالة يتناول الكل فيحتمل أن يكون الصواب استحسن هذا الدليل ابن الحاجب مع المخالف، وقال بعض المعتزلة ينعقد الإجماع باتفاق الأكثر؛ من للإجماع اللاحق أي الذي انعقد وارتفع به الخلاف السابق على رأي محمد له. (القمر) لأجل الاختلاف السابق فلم يتحقق الإجماع اللاحق؛ لأن شرط انعقاده عدم الاختلاف السابق في رواية الكرخي يه، فوقع القضاء في فصل مجتهد فيه فينفذ وأما عدم نفاذه على ظاهر الرواية عند الإمام الأعظم مه أنه ينعقد الإجماع اللاحق وإن وقع خلاف في السابق فليس لعدم صحة الإجماع اللاحق إذا سبق فيه الخلاف، بل لأن هذا الإجماع الذي تقدمه خلاف عند كثير من العلماء ليس بإجماع، وعند من جعله إجماعا هو إجماع فيه شبهة حتى لا يكفّر جاحده ولا يُضلّل، فهو بمنزلة خبر الواحد، فصادف قضاء القاضي ببيع أم الولد محلاً مجتهدا فيه غير مخالف للإجماع القطعي، فينفذ قضاؤه. كذا في بعض الشروح. (القمر) اجتماع الكل: أي جميع المجتهدين، وقيل: أقل ما ينعقد به ثلاثة وإليه مال السرخسي؛ لأنه أقل الجماعة، وقيل: اثنان؛ لأنه أقل الجمع، وقيل: لو لم يبق من المجتهدين إلا واحد يكون قوله إجماعا؛ لأنه عند الانفراد يصدق عليه لفظ الأمة كما قال الله تعالى: ﴿ إِنَّ إِبْرَاهِيمَ كَانَ أُمَّةً قَانِتَا لِلَّهِ، (النحل:١٢٠) كذا قال ابن الملك.(القمر) اجتماع الكل إلخ فإجماع الأكثر ليس بإجماع على المختار لانتفاء الكل الذي هو مناط العصمة، ثم اختلفوا في أن إجماع الأكثر ليس حجة أصلاً كما أنه ليس بإجماع، وقيل: هو حجة ظنية غير الإجماع.(السنبلي) يتناول الكل: فإذا خالف واحد لم يتحقق الكل. (القمر) ما أن هذا الحديث متواتر المعنى، وأخرج الترمذي رقم: ٢١٦٧ ، باب ما جاء في لزوم الجماعة، عن ابن عمر رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم قال : إن الله لا يجمع أمتي أو قال: أمة محمد على ضلالة.
Statement of the Condition of Consensus. The condition is the gathering of all, and the opposition of one is a preventer like the opposition of the majority, meaning at the time of the formation of consensus, if one dissents, his dissent is considered and consensus is not formed, because the word 'community' (al-ummah) in his saying (peace be upon him): 'My community will not agree on error' includes all. So it is possible that the correct view is that... Ibn al-Hajib considered this evidence good even with the dissenter. And some Mu'tazilites say that consensus is formed by agreement of the majority. (al-Qamar) Due to the prior disagreement, the later consensus was not realized, because its condition is the absence of prior disagreement in the narration of al-Karkhi. So the ruling occurred in a matter of ijtihad and is therefore executed. As for its non-execution according to the apparent narration of the Great Imam, it is that the later consensus is formed even if disagreement occurred earlier; it is not due to the invalidity of the later consensus if disagreement preceded it, but rather because this consensus which was preceded by disagreement is, according to many scholars, not consensus, and according to those who consider it consensus, it is consensus with doubt, so that one who denies it is not deemed an unbeliever nor led astray. It is like a solitary report (khabar al-wahid). So the judge's ruling to sell the umm walad occurred in a matter of ijtihad not conflicting with definitive consensus, so his ruling is executed. Thus in some commentaries. (al-Qamar) 'Gathering of all': meaning all mujtahids. And it is said: The minimum for consensus is three, and al-Sarakhsi inclined to that, because it is the minimum of a group. And it is said: two, because it is the minimum of a plural. And it is said: If only one mujtahid remains, his statement is consensus, because when alone, the term ummah applies to him, as Allah said: 'Indeed, Abraham was a community [ummah] obedient to Allah' (al-Nahl 16:120). Thus said Ibn al-Malik. (al-Qamar) 'Gathering of all' etc. So consensus of the majority is not consensus according to the chosen view, due to the absence of the whole which is the basis of infallibility. Then they differed: Is the consensus of the majority not a proof at all just as it is not consensus? And it is said: it is a probable proof (hujja zanniya) other than consensus. (al-Sunbuli) 'Includes all': so if one dissents, the whole is not realized. (al-Qamar) And that this hadith is mutawatir in meaning, and al-Tirmidhi narrated number 2167, chapter on adhering to the group, from Ibn 'Umar that the Messenger of Allah said: 'Indeed, Allah will not bring my community together—or he said: the community of Muhammad—on error.'
Source pages p. 628

Commentary
This passage explains the condition for the validity of Ijma': consensus of all mujtahids (ijma' al-kull). It begins by stating that the condition is the agreement of all, and that a single dissenter prevents consensus just as a majority dissent does. The proof is the hadith 'My community will not agree on error' which includes all members. The text then mentions that some Mu'tazilites allow consensus by majority, but the correct view is that majority agreement is not consensus. It further discusses the minimum number required for consensus: three (preferred by al-Sarakhsi), two, or even one (based on the verse about Abraham being an ummah). The text also returns to the earlier issue of subsequent consensus, explaining that according to one narration of al-Karkhi, the condition for subsequent consensus is the absence of prior disagreement, but according to the apparent narration of Abu Hanifa, subsequent consensus is valid even if there was prior disagreement, but such consensus is considered weak (like khabar al-wahid) and does not reach the level of definitive consensus, so a judge's ruling contrary to it may be upheld if it is a matter of ijtihad. The passage concludes with the hadith reference from Tirmidhi, noting that it is mutawatir in meaning. This lesson emphasizes the strict requirement of unanimity for binding consensus and the different opinions on what constitutes 'all'.

Key Terms
اجتماع الكل (ijtima' al-kull): The agreement of all mujtahids; the condition for ijma'.
خلاف الواحد (khilaf al-wahid): The dissent of a single mujtahid; it prevents the formation of consensus.
أمة (ummah): Community; in the hadith, it refers to the entire body of mujtahids. The term can also apply to a single person when alone (as in the verse on Abraham).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi view stated in this passage, what is required for the formation of Ijma'?
A) Agreement of the majority of mujtahids is sufficient.
B) Agreement of all mujtahids is required; a single dissenter prevents it.
C) Agreement of at least three mujtahids is required.
D) Agreement of at least two mujtahids is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
The condition for binding Ijma' is the unanimous agreement of all mujtahids; a single dissenter prevents the consensus from forming, as per the Hanafi interpretation of the hadith and the Quranic usage of 'ummah'.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
6 min
The Definitive Nature of Ijma' (Consensus)
Stating the definitive hukm of Ijma' and its limits

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that Ijma' is a definitive proof (qat'i) in principle, identify the conditions under which its denier becomes a disbeliever, and explain the exception of silent Ijma'.

Core Idea
Ijma' provides certainty like the Qur'an, but its denier is not always a disbeliever — only if the matter is from dharuriyyat al-din.

In this passage from Noor al-Anwaar, the author establishes the fundamental hukm of Ijma': it is a definitive proof (qat'i) that yields certainty in legal matters. However, this certainty can be obstructed in certain cases, such as silent Ijma'. The text also delineates the scope of takfir for those who reject an Ijma'-based ruling — a nuanced position that distinguishes between necessary and non-necessary religious matters.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling (hukm) of Ijma'
The passage states that Ijma' in legal matters yields certainty (yaqeen) and definitiveness (qat'iyyah) in origin.
This is the default position.
2
Note the exception: silent Ijma'
Silent Ijma' (ijma' sukuti) does not produce certainty due to an obstacle ('aarid).
Only explicit Ijma' is qat'i.
3
Understand the consequence for deniers
A denier of a ruling established by definitive Ijma' is a disbeliever, but only if the matter is from the necessities of religion (dharuriyyat al-din) known to both elite and common people.
If it is not from dharuriyyat al-din, a corrupt interpretation can prevent takfir.
4
Apply the nuance
The Rawafid who denied Abu Bakr's caliphate were not declared disbelievers by some because they had a false interpretation, indicating that a corrupt ta'wil can prevent takfir if the matter is not from dharuriyyat al-din.
This shows the importance of intention and interpretation.

Source Text

بيان حكم الإجماع
باب الإجماع لأن الحق مع الجماعة؛ لقوله عليه: "يد الله على الجماعة فمن شدّ شُدّ في النار"، * والجواب أن معناه بعد تحقق الإجماع من شد وخرج منه دخل في النار.
بيان حكم الإجماع أي الإجماع وحكمه في الأصل أن يثبت المراد به شرعًا على سبيل اليقين يعني أن الإجماع في الأمور الشرعية في الأصل يفيد اليقين والقطعية، فيكفر جاحده وإن كان في بعض المواضع بسبب العارض لا يفيد القطع كالإجماع السكوني لقوله تعالى: بعد تحقق الإجماع إلخ بناءً على أن هذا القول يمنع المخالفة بعد الموافقة؛ لأن قوله : "شَدّ" من "شَدّ البعير" إذا توحش بعد ما كان أهليًا. (السنبلي وحكمه أي حكم الإجماع، أي الأثر الثابت به في الأصل، أي في أصل وضعه. (القمر) شرعًا حال من المراد بمعنى مشروعًا، قال ابن الملك: إنما قيد الحكم بالشرعي؛ لأنه هو محل الانعقاد، لا أمر الدنيا كأمر الحرب ،وغيره فإنهم إذا أجمعوا على الحرب في موضع معين قيل: لا ينعقد إجماعًا. (القمر) يفيد اليقين إلخ بحيث لا يحتمل الجانب المخالف أصلاً، لا احتمالاً ناشيًا بلا دليل ولا احتمالا ناشيًا مع دليل كإفادة الكتاب والسنة المتواترة. (القمر) فيكفّر جاحده: أي جاحد الحكم الثابت بالإجماع، كذا عند مشائخ بخارا وبلخ حتى حكموا بكفر الروافض؛ لأنهم أنكروا إمامة أبي بكر الصديق الله التي ثبتت بالإجماع، وقال الشيخ الأكبر محي الدين ابن العربي: إن الشخص مادام يتمسك بالكتاب والسنة لا يكفّر وإن كان تأويله فاسدًا، فلو كان المجمع عليه من ضروريات الدين بحيث يعرفه الخاصة والعامة فيكفّر جاحده، ولو لم يكن كذالك فمنكره لو أنكر بتأويل وإن كان تأويله فاسدًا لا يكفّر؛ لأنه ما أنكر الدين المحمدي بزعمه ،وهواه ولذا قيل: إن لزوم الكفر ليس بكفر، وإلزام الكفر كفر، والروافض أنكروا إمامة أبي بكر الصديق له بتأويل باطل، وهو أن عليا كرم الله وجهه بايعه بالتقية، فلم يتحقق الإجماع؛ فلذا لا يُكفّرون، وهذا التأويل باطل؛ فإنه قد تواتر منه أن وخلوص اعتقاده، وهو كان أشجع الصحابة لله، فالتقية انحطاط شأنه، وقيل: إن جاحد نكاح المتعة لم يكفّر مع الإجماع على بطلانه؛ لأنه مما لا يعرفه إلا الخاصة كذا نقل العلي القاري له، وللتفصيل مقام آخر.(القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ هذا دليل لقوله : يفيد اليقين. (القمر) لقوله تعالى: والدليل العقلي أنا وجدنا اتفاق كل عصر على تخطية المخالف للإجماع بالقطع، فكون الإجماع صوابًا مطابقًا للواقع مركوز في أذهانهم ومقطوع عندهم، وهذا القطع لا يحصل إلا عن قاطع ظهر لهم مثل ظهور الشمس نصف النهار ، فلزم حجيته قطعا. (السنبلي)
أخرجه الترمذي رقم: ٢١٦٧ ، باب ما جاء في لزوم الجماعة عن ابن عمر
بيعة كان بصميم قلبه
بيان حكم الإجماع
﴿وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطاً لِتَكُونُوا شُهَدَاءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ﴾ وصفهم بالوسطية، وهي العدالة، فيكون إجماعهم حجة، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ﴾ (آل عمران: ١١٠) والخيرية إنما يكون باعتبار كمالهم في الدين، فيكون إجماعهم حجة، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرَ سَبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ نُوَلِّهِ مَا تَوَلَّى﴾ (النساء: ١١٥) فجعلت مخالفة المؤمنين مثل مخالفة الرسول، فيكون إجماعهم كخبر الرسول حجة قطعية وأمثاله، وقد ضلّ بعض المعتزلة والروافض فقالوا: إن الإجماع ليس بحجة؛ وكذلك: أي كما جعلنا قبلتكم أفضل القبل جعلناكم أمة وَسَطًا أي خيارًا أو عدولاً لتكونوا شهداء على الناس يوم القيامة بتبليغ الأنبياء علية الأحكام الإلهية إليهم عند جحودهم بتبليغهم ، ويكون الرسول عليكم شهيدًا بعد التكم، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) فيكون إجماعهم حجة فإن العدل هو الراسخ على الصراط المستقيم، وليس فيه الزيغ عن سواء السبيل، ولقائل أن يقول: إن العدالة لا تنافي الخطأ في الاجتهاد؛ إذ هو ليس فسقا، بل المجتهد المخطئ مأجور ، فلا دليل في هذه الآية على قطعية إجماع المجتهدين من عصر واحد (القمر) كنتم خير أمة: الخطاب إلى تمام الأمة المحمدية فللموجودين في ذلك الزمان أي الصحابة لم تنجيزا، وللمعدومين في ذلك الزمان عند الوجود أخرجت أي أظهرت للناس. (القمر) فيكون إجماعهم حجة: إذ لو لم يكن إجماعهم حقًا وحجة لكان ضلالاً فكيف يكون الأمة الضالة خير الأمم؟ وقال صاحب "التلويح": إن الضلال في بعض الأحكام بناء على الخطاء في الاجتهاد بعد بذل الوسع لا ينافي كون المؤمنين العالمين بالشرائع الممتثلين للأوامر خير الأمم، وبعد التسليم فلا دلالة قطعًا في الآية على قطعية إجماع المجتهدين من عصر واحد.(القمر)
نوله ما تَولّى أي نجعله واليا لما توَلّاه من الضلال بأن نخلي بينه وبينه في الدنيا.(القمر) مثل مخالفة الرسول إلخ فإنه توعد على متابعة غير سبيل المؤمنين كما توعد على مخالفة الرسول باستيجاب النار، فكان إتباع غير سبيل المؤمنين حرامًا، فوجب إتباع سبيل المؤمنين، فكان الإجماع حجة فإنه سبيلهم؛ إذ السبيل ما يختاره الإنسان قولاً وعملاً ولقائل أن يقول : إن اتباع غير سبيل المؤمنين هو مشاقة الرسول بعينه، والفرق الاعتباري مفهوما يكفي لصحة العطف كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿أَطِيعُوا اللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا الرَّسُولَ﴾ (النساء:٥٩) مع أن طاعة الرسول عين طاعة الله تعالى في الوجود الخارجي، فحينئذٍ لا أثر لثبوت الإجماع من هذه الآية، كذا قال صاحب "التوضيح"، وقدح عليه صاحب "التلويح" بأن العطف وإن كان صحيحًا لكن سبيل المؤمنين عام لا مخصص له بما ثبت إتيان الرسول به، فلا ضرورة للتخصيص مع أن حمل الكلام على الفائدة الجديدة أولى.(القمر) بعض المعتزلة إلخ وكذا الخوارج ، وهم شرذمة قليلة من الحمقاء، لا يعتد بهم لأنهم حادثون الاتفاق يشككون في ضروريات الدين مثل السوفسطائية في الضروريات العقلية. (السنبلي)
Explanation of the ruling of Ijma' / Chapter of Ijma' because the truth is with the group; due to his saying (peace be upon him): "The hand of Allah is upon the group, so whoever separates, will separate into the Fire." * The answer is that its meaning is after the realization of Ijma', whoever separates and deviates from it enters the Fire. / Explanation of the ruling of Ijma': i.e., Ijma' and its ruling in origin is that what is intended by it is established legally on the basis of certainty, meaning that Ijma' in legal matters in origin benefits certainty and definitiveness, so its denier is considered a disbeliever, although in some instances due to an obstacle it does not benefit certainty, such as silent Ijma'. Due to His (Exalted) saying: 'After the realization of Ijma' etc.' based on the fact that this saying prevents opposition after agreement; because his saying (peace be upon him) "shadd" is from "shadd al-ba'ir" when it becomes wild after being domesticated. (al-Sunbuli) And its ruling: i.e., the ruling of Ijma', i.e., the effect established by it in origin, i.e., in its original establishment. (al-Qamar) Legally (shar'an) is a state of the intended meaning, i.e., legislated. Ibn al-Malik said: The ruling is restricted to legal matters because it is the subject of contract, not worldly matters like war and others; for if they agree on war in a particular place, it is said that Ijma' is not contracted. (al-Qamar) It benefits certainty etc. such that it does not admit the opposing possibility at all, neither a possibility arising without evidence nor a possibility arising with evidence, like the benefit of the Book and Mutawatir Sunnah. (al-Qamar) So its denier is considered a disbeliever: i.e., the denier of the ruling established by Ijma'. This is the opinion of the scholars of Bukhara and Balkh, to the extent that they ruled the Rawafid as disbelievers because they denied the caliphate of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) which was established by Ijma'. Shaykh al-Akbar Muhyi al-Din Ibn Arabi said: As long as a person holds on to the Book and Sunnah, he is not considered a disbeliever even if his interpretation is corrupt. If the matter agreed upon is among the necessities of the religion (dharuriyyat al-din) such that both the elite and common people know it, then its denier is considered a disbeliever. But if not, then one who denies it due to an interpretation, even if his interpretation is corrupt, is not considered a disbeliever because he did not deny the Muhammadan religion according to his claim and desire. Hence it is said: The implication of disbelief is not disbelief, and declaring someone a disbeliever is disbelief. The Rawafid denied the caliphate of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) due to a false interpretation, namely that Ali (may Allah honor his face) paid allegiance under duress (taqiyya), so Ijma' was not realized; therefore they are not considered disbelievers. This interpretation is false; for it is mutawatir from him (Ali) that his allegiance was with sincerity and pure belief, and he was the bravest of the Companions for Allah's sake, so taqiyya would demean his status. And it is said that the denier of temporary marriage (mut'a) is not considered a disbeliever despite Ijma' on its invalidity because it is only known by the elite, as transmitted by al-'Ali al-Qari. And there is another place for detail. (al-Qamar) Due to His (Exalted) saying etc.: this is a proof for his statement that it benefits certainty. (al-Qamar) Due to His (Exalted) saying: and the rational proof is that we find that every age agrees with certainty on the error of the one who opposes Ijma'. So the fact that Ijma' is correct and corresponds to reality is ingrained in their minds and certain for them. And this certainty does not come except from something decisive that has appeared to them like the appearance of the sun at midday, so its authority is necessarily decisive. (al-Sunbuli) / (Hadith) narrated by al-Tirmidhi no. 2167, chapter on adhering to the group from Ibn Umar. / His allegiance was with the core of his heart. / Explanation of the ruling of Ijma': / And thus we have made you a middle nation that you may be witnesses over mankind. (Quran 2:143) He described them with middle-ness, which is justice, so their Ijma' is proof. And similarly His saying: And you are the best nation produced for mankind. (Aal Imran 3:110) And goodness is only due to their perfection in the religion, so their Ijma' is proof. And similarly His saying: And whoever opposes the Messenger after guidance has become clear to him and follows other than the way of the believers, We will turn him to what he has turned to. (al-Nisa 4:115) So opposing the believers is made like opposing the Messenger, so their Ijma' is like the report of the Messenger, a definitive proof, and similar [verses]. And some of the Mu'tazila and Rawafid have strayed and said that Ijma' is not proof. / And thus: just as We made your qibla the best of qiblas, We have made you a middle nation, i.e., chosen or just, that you may be witnesses over mankind on the Day of Judgment regarding the conveyance of divine rulings by the prophets to them when they deny their conveyance, and the Messenger will be a witness over you after that, as al-Baydawi said. (al-Qamar) So their Ijma' is proof, for the just person is firm upon the straight path without deviation from the right way. And one may say: Justice does not preclude error in ijtihad, for it is not sin; rather the mistaken mujtahid is rewarded. So there is no proof in this verse for the definitiveness of the Ijma' of the mujtahids of one era. (al-Qamar) You are the best nation: the address is to the entire Muhammadan community, for those present at that time, i.e., the Companions, as a completed act, and for those not present at that time when they come into existence. Brought forth: i.e., shown to mankind. (al-Qamar) So their Ijma' is proof: for if their Ijma' were not truth and proof, then it would be misguidance. So how can the misguided nation be the best of nations? And the author of al-Talwih said: Misguidance in some rulings based on error in ijtihad after exhausting one's effort does not negate that the believing scholars who follow the commands are the best of nations. And even if this is accepted, there is certainly no indication in the verse for the definitiveness of the Ijma' of the mujtahids of one era. (al-Qamar) / We will turn him to what he has turned to: i.e., We will make him a guardian of the misguidance he has turned to by leaving him to it in this world. (al-Qamar) Like opposing the Messenger etc.: for He threatened following other than the way of the believers just as He threatened opposing the Messenger with the obligation of Hellfire. So following other than the way of the believers is forbidden, so following the way of the believers is obligatory. Thus Ijma' is proof, for it is their way; since the way is what one chooses in speech and action. And one may say: Following other than the way of the believers is the same as opposing the Messenger, and the conceptual distinction in meaning is sufficient for the validity of conjunction, as in His saying: Obey Allah and obey the Messenger (al-Nisa 4:59) even though obedience to the Messenger is exactly obedience to Allah in external existence. In that case, there is no effect for establishing Ijma' from this verse, as said by the author of al-Tawdih. And the author of al-Talwih criticized him saying: Although the conjunction is valid, the way of the believers is general with no specification based on what the Messenger has brought, so there is no need for specification, and interpreting the speech to convey new benefit is preferable. (al-Qamar) Some of the Mu'tazila etc.: and also the Khawarij, and they are a small band of fools, not taken into account because they are later [sect] who cast doubt on the necessities of religion, like the Sophists [cast doubt] on rational necessities. (al-Sunbuli)
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage, from the chapter on Ijma' in Noor al-Anwaar, states the ruling (hukm) of Ijma' (consensus) and its proofs. The author begins by asserting that Ijma' in legal matters provides certainty (yaqeen) and definitiveness (qat'iyyah) in principle, such that a denier of a ruling established by definitive Ijma' is considered a disbeliever (kafir). However, exceptions exist due to obstacles like 'ijma' sukuti' (silent consensus). The passage then provides Quranic proofs: (1) Quran 2:143 describing the Muslim community as a 'middle nation' (ummatan wasatan), interpreted as just, so their consensus is authoritative. (2) Quran 3:110 calling them 'the best nation', implying their consensus cannot be wrong. (3) Quran 4:115 warning against following 'other than the way of the believers', equating it to opposing the Messenger, thus establishing Ijma' as a definitive proof. The author then addresses objections from some Mu'tazila and Rawafid who deny Ijma' as a proof, dismissing them as a misguided few. The commentary (indicated by al-Qamar, al-Sunbuli, etc.) discusses nuances: the ruling applies only to legal matters, not worldly affairs like war; the certainty of Ijma' admits no contrary possibility; the takfir of deniers applies only if the matter is from the necessities of religion (dharuriyyat al-din) known to all; otherwise, a denier with a corrupt interpretation is not takfir. The passage also includes a rational proof: that all eras agree on the error of those opposing Ijma', and this certainty can only come from a decisive basis. The Hanafi position is that Ijma' is a qat'i proof, and its authority is from dharuriyyat al-din.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-ijma'): The consensus of the mujtahids of the ummah on a legal ruling after the death of the Prophet (peace be upon him).
اليقين (al-yaqeen): Certainty that admits no opposite possibility, like the certainty from the Book and Mutawatir Sunnah.
قطع (qat'): Definitiveness; the quality of being free from doubt.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi usul text, when does the denier of a ruling established by Ijma' become a disbeliever?
A) Whenever he denies any Ijma' regardless of the issue.
B) Only when the Ijma' is on a matter from the necessities of religion (dharuriyyat al-din) known to both elite and common people.
C) Only when the Ijma' is 'ijma' sukuti' (silent consensus).
D) Never, because Ijma' is only a probable proof.

Key Takeaway
Ijma' is a definitive proof in principle, but its binding force for takfir is limited to matters from the essentials of religion.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
8 min
The Evidential Proofs for Ijma' from the Quran and Reason
Presenting the primary sources (Quran and rational) for the authority of Ijma'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Quranic verses cited as evidence for Ijma', explain their wajh al-dalalah, and evaluate the rational proof invoking universal agreement.

Core Idea
Quran 4:115 equates following 'other than the way of the believers' with opposing the Messenger, making Ijma' as binding as a prophetic command.

This passage presents the scriptural and rational foundations for the authority of Ijma'. The author cites three key verses: (1) 2:143 – describing the ummah as 'wasatan', interpreted as just, thus their consensus is proof; (2) 3:110 – calling them 'khayra ummah', implying their Ijma' is truth; and (3) 4:115 – threatening those who follow other than the believers' way, equating it to opposing the Messenger. A rational argument is also given: the universal agreement on the error of anyone who opposes Ijma' indicates the certainty of Ijma' as proof. The text also addresses objections raised against these proofs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the first verse (2:143) and its interpretation
'Wasatan' means just/balanced, so the ummah's testimony is trustworthy; therefore their Ijma' is authoritative.
Based on al-Baydawi's tafsir.
2
Identify the second verse (3:110) and its interpretation
'Khayra ummah' means best nation; if their Ijma' could be wrong, they wouldn't be the best, so their Ijma' must be truth.
Counter objection: error in ijtihad does not negate being the best community.
3
Identify the third verse (4:115) as the strongest proof
The threat on following 'other than the way of the believers' is equated to opposing the Messenger, establishing that the way of the believers (i.e., Ijma') must be followed obligatorily.
Objection: 'other than the way' may refer to the path of all believers without exception.
4
Analyze the rational proof
All ages agree that opposing Ijma' is error; this universal agreement itself is certain, proving that Ijma' is a decisive proof.
This argument is used to refute those who deny Ijma' altogether.
5
Consider the objections and Hanafi responses
The text notes that some scholars criticize the Quranic proofs as not definitively establishing Ijma'. The author presents counterarguments from al-Talwih and others, ultimately reaffirming the Hanafi stance.
The debate shows the depth of usul reasoning.

بيان حكم الإجماع
باب الإجماع لأن الحق مع الجماعة؛ لقوله عليه: "يد الله على الجماعة فمن شدّ شُدّ في النار"، * والجواب أن معناه بعد تحقق الإجماع من شد وخرج منه دخل في النار.
بيان حكم الإجماع أي الإجماع وحكمه في الأصل أن يثبت المراد به شرعًا على سبيل اليقين يعني أن الإجماع في الأمور الشرعية في الأصل يفيد اليقين والقطعية، فيكفر جاحده وإن كان في بعض المواضع بسبب العارض لا يفيد القطع كالإجماع السكوني لقوله تعالى: بعد تحقق الإجماع إلخ بناءً على أن هذا القول يمنع المخالفة بعد الموافقة؛ لأن قوله : "شَدّ" من "شَدّ البعير" إذا توحش بعد ما كان أهليًا. (السنبلي وحكمه أي حكم الإجماع، أي الأثر الثابت به في الأصل، أي في أصل وضعه. (القمر) شرعًا حال من المراد بمعنى مشروعًا، قال ابن الملك: إنما قيد الحكم بالشرعي؛ لأنه هو محل الانعقاد، لا أمر الدنيا كأمر الحرب ،وغيره فإنهم إذا أجمعوا على الحرب في موضع معين قيل: لا ينعقد إجماعًا. (القمر) يفيد اليقين إلخ بحيث لا يحتمل الجانب المخالف أصلاً، لا احتمالاً ناشيًا بلا دليل ولا احتمالا ناشيًا مع دليل كإفادة الكتاب والسنة المتواترة. (القمر) فيكفّر جاحده: أي جاحد الحكم الثابت بالإجماع، كذا عند مشائخ بخارا وبلخ حتى حكموا بكفر الروافض؛ لأنهم أنكروا إمامة أبي بكر الصديق الله التي ثبتت بالإجماع، وقال الشيخ الأكبر محي الدين ابن العربي: إن الشخص مادام يتمسك بالكتاب والسنة لا يكفّر وإن كان تأويله فاسدًا، فلو كان المجمع عليه من ضروريات الدين بحيث يعرفه الخاصة والعامة فيكفّر جاحده، ولو لم يكن كذالك فمنكره لو أنكر بتأويل وإن كان تأويله فاسدًا لا يكفّر؛ لأنه ما أنكر الدين المحمدي بزعمه ،وهواه ولذا قيل: إن لزوم الكفر ليس بكفر، وإلزام الكفر كفر، والروافض أنكروا إمامة أبي بكر الصديق له بتأويل باطل، وهو أن عليا كرم الله وجهه بايعه بالتقية، فلم يتحقق الإجماع؛ فلذا لا يُكفّرون، وهذا التأويل باطل؛ فإنه قد تواتر منه أن وخلوص اعتقاده، وهو كان أشجع الصحابة لله، فالتقية انحطاط شأنه، وقيل: إن جاحد نكاح المتعة لم يكفّر مع الإجماع على بطلانه؛ لأنه مما لا يعرفه إلا الخاصة كذا نقل العلي القاري له، وللتفصيل مقام آخر.(القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ هذا دليل لقوله : يفيد اليقين. (القمر) لقوله تعالى: والدليل العقلي أنا وجدنا اتفاق كل عصر على تخطية المخالف للإجماع بالقطع، فكون الإجماع صوابًا مطابقًا للواقع مركوز في أذهانهم ومقطوع عندهم، وهذا القطع لا يحصل إلا عن قاطع ظهر لهم مثل ظهور الشمس نصف النهار ، فلزم حجيته قطعا. (السنبلي)
أخرجه الترمذي رقم: ٢١٦٧ ، باب ما جاء في لزوم الجماعة عن ابن عمر
بيعة كان بصميم قلبه
بيان حكم الإجماع
﴿وَكَذَلِكَ جَعَلْنَاكُمْ أُمَّةً وَسَطاً لِتَكُونُوا شُهَدَاءَ عَلَى النَّاسِ﴾ وصفهم بالوسطية، وهي العدالة، فيكون إجماعهم حجة، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَكُنتُمْ خَيْرَ أُمَّةٍ أُخْرِجَتْ لِلنَّاسِ﴾ (آل عمران: ١١٠) والخيرية إنما يكون باعتبار كمالهم في الدين، فيكون إجماعهم حجة، وكذا قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَنْ يُشَاقِقِ الرَّسُولَ مِنْ بَعْدِ مَا تَبَيَّنَ لَهُ الْهُدَى وَيَتَّبِعْ غَيْرَ سَبِيلِ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ نُوَلِّهِ مَا تَوَلَّى﴾ (النساء: ١١٥) فجعلت مخالفة المؤمنين مثل مخالفة الرسول، فيكون إجماعهم كخبر الرسول حجة قطعية وأمثاله، وقد ضلّ بعض المعتزلة والروافض فقالوا: إن الإجماع ليس بحجة؛ وكذلك: أي كما جعلنا قبلتكم أفضل القبل جعلناكم أمة وَسَطًا أي خيارًا أو عدولاً لتكونوا شهداء على الناس يوم القيامة بتبليغ الأنبياء علية الأحكام الإلهية إليهم عند جحودهم بتبليغهم ، ويكون الرسول عليكم شهيدًا بعد التكم، كذا قال البيضاوي. (القمر) فيكون إجماعهم حجة فإن العدل هو الراسخ على الصراط المستقيم، وليس فيه الزيغ عن سواء السبيل، ولقائل أن يقول: إن العدالة لا تنافي الخطأ في الاجتهاد؛ إذ هو ليس فسقا، بل المجتهد المخطئ مأجور ، فلا دليل في هذه الآية على قطعية إجماع المجتهدين من عصر واحد (القمر) كنتم خير أمة: الخطاب إلى تمام الأمة المحمدية فللموجودين في ذلك الزمان أي الصحابة لم تنجيزا، وللمعدومين في ذلك الزمان عند الوجود أخرجت أي أظهرت للناس. (القمر) فيكون إجماعهم حجة: إذ لو لم يكن إجماعهم حقًا وحجة لكان ضلالاً فكيف يكون الأمة الضالة خير الأمم؟ وقال صاحب "التلويح": إن الضلال في بعض الأحكام بناء على الخطاء في الاجتهاد بعد بذل الوسع لا ينافي كون المؤمنين العالمين بالشرائع الممتثلين للأوامر خير الأمم، وبعد التسليم فلا دلالة قطعًا في الآية على قطعية إجماع المجتهدين من عصر واحد.(القمر)
نوله ما تَولّى أي نجعله واليا لما توَلّاه من الضلال بأن نخلي بينه وبينه في الدنيا.(القمر) مثل مخالفة الرسول إلخ فإنه توعد على متابعة غير سبيل المؤمنين كما توعد على مخالفة الرسول باستيجاب النار، فكان إتباع غير سبيل المؤمنين حرامًا، فوجب إتباع سبيل المؤمنين، فكان الإجماع حجة فإنه سبيلهم؛ إذ السبيل ما يختاره الإنسان قولاً وعملاً ولقائل أن يقول : إن اتباع غير سبيل المؤمنين هو مشاقة الرسول بعينه، والفرق الاعتباري مفهوما يكفي لصحة العطف كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿أَطِيعُوا اللَّهَ وَأَطِيعُوا الرَّسُولَ﴾ (النساء:٥٩) مع أن طاعة الرسول عين طاعة الله تعالى في الوجود الخارجي، فحينئذٍ لا أثر لثبوت الإجماع من هذه الآية، كذا قال صاحب "التوضيح"، وقدح عليه صاحب "التلويح" بأن العطف وإن كان صحيحًا لكن سبيل المؤمنين عام لا مخصص له بما ثبت إتيان الرسول به، فلا ضرورة للتخصيص مع أن حمل الكلام على الفائدة الجديدة أولى.(القمر) بعض المعتزلة إلخ وكذا الخوارج ، وهم شرذمة قليلة من الحمقاء، لا يعتد بهم لأنهم حادثون الاتفاق يشككون في ضروريات الدين مثل السوفسطائية في الضروريات العقلية. (السنبلي)
Explanation of the ruling of Ijma' / Chapter of Ijma' because the truth is with the group; due to his saying (peace be upon him): "The hand of Allah is upon the group, so whoever separates, will separate into the Fire." * The answer is that its meaning is after the realization of Ijma', whoever separates and deviates from it enters the Fire. / Explanation of the ruling of Ijma': i.e., Ijma' and its ruling in origin is that what is intended by it is established legally on the basis of certainty, meaning that Ijma' in legal matters in origin benefits certainty and definitiveness, so its denier is considered a disbeliever, although in some instances due to an obstacle it does not benefit certainty, such as silent Ijma'. Due to His (Exalted) saying: 'After the realization of Ijma' etc.' based on the fact that this saying prevents opposition after agreement; because his saying (peace be upon him) "shadd" is from "shadd al-ba'ir" when it becomes wild after being domesticated. (al-Sunbuli) And its ruling: i.e., the ruling of Ijma', i.e., the effect established by it in origin, i.e., in its original establishment. (al-Qamar) Legally (shar'an) is a state of the intended meaning, i.e., legislated. Ibn al-Malik said: The ruling is restricted to legal matters because it is the subject of contract, not worldly matters like war and others; for if they agree on war in a particular place, it is said that Ijma' is not contracted. (al-Qamar) It benefits certainty etc. such that it does not admit the opposing possibility at all, neither a possibility arising without evidence nor a possibility arising with evidence, like the benefit of the Book and Mutawatir Sunnah. (al-Qamar) So its denier is considered a disbeliever: i.e., the denier of the ruling established by Ijma'. This is the opinion of the scholars of Bukhara and Balkh, to the extent that they ruled the Rawafid as disbelievers because they denied the caliphate of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) which was established by Ijma'. Shaykh al-Akbar Muhyi al-Din Ibn Arabi said: As long as a person holds on to the Book and Sunnah, he is not considered a disbeliever even if his interpretation is corrupt. If the matter agreed upon is among the necessities of the religion (dharuriyyat al-din) such that both the elite and common people know it, then its denier is considered a disbeliever. But if not, then one who denies it due to an interpretation, even if his interpretation is corrupt, is not considered a disbeliever because he did not deny the Muhammadan religion according to his claim and desire. Hence it is said: The implication of disbelief is not disbelief, and declaring someone a disbeliever is disbelief. The Rawafid denied the caliphate of Abu Bakr al-Siddiq (may Allah be pleased with him) due to a false interpretation, namely that Ali (may Allah honor his face) paid allegiance under duress (taqiyya), so Ijma' was not realized; therefore they are not considered disbelievers. This interpretation is false; for it is mutawatir from him (Ali) that his allegiance was with sincerity and pure belief, and he was the bravest of the Companions for Allah's sake, so taqiyya would demean his status. And it is said that the denier of temporary marriage (mut'a) is not considered a disbeliever despite Ijma' on its invalidity because it is only known by the elite, as transmitted by al-'Ali al-Qari. And there is another place for detail. (al-Qamar) Due to His (Exalted) saying etc.: this is a proof for his statement that it benefits certainty. (al-Qamar) Due to His (Exalted) saying: and the rational proof is that we find that every age agrees with certainty on the error of the one who opposes Ijma'. So the fact that Ijma' is correct and corresponds to reality is ingrained in their minds and certain for them. And this certainty does not come except from something decisive that has appeared to them like the appearance of the sun at midday, so its authority is necessarily decisive. (al-Sunbuli) / (Hadith) narrated by al-Tirmidhi no. 2167, chapter on adhering to the group from Ibn Umar. / His allegiance was with the core of his heart. / Explanation of the ruling of Ijma': / And thus we have made you a middle nation that you may be witnesses over mankind. (Quran 2:143) He described them with middle-ness, which is justice, so their Ijma' is proof. And similarly His saying: And you are the best nation produced for mankind. (Aal Imran 3:110) And goodness is only due to their perfection in the religion, so their Ijma' is proof. And similarly His saying: And whoever opposes the Messenger after guidance has become clear to him and follows other than the way of the believers, We will turn him to what he has turned to. (al-Nisa 4:115) So opposing the believers is made like opposing the Messenger, so their Ijma' is like the report of the Messenger, a definitive proof, and similar [verses]. And some of the Mu'tazila and Rawafid have strayed and said that Ijma' is not proof. / And thus: just as We made your qibla the best of qiblas, We have made you a middle nation, i.e., chosen or just, that you may be witnesses over mankind on the Day of Judgment regarding the conveyance of divine rulings by the prophets to them when they deny their conveyance, and the Messenger will be a witness over you after that, as al-Baydawi said. (al-Qamar) So their Ijma' is proof, for the just person is firm upon the straight path without deviation from the right way. And one may say: Justice does not preclude error in ijtihad, for it is not sin; rather the mistaken mujtahid is rewarded. So there is no proof in this verse for the definitiveness of the Ijma' of the mujtahids of one era. (al-Qamar) You are the best nation: the address is to the entire Muhammadan community, for those present at that time, i.e., the Companions, as a completed act, and for those not present at that time when they come into existence. Brought forth: i.e., shown to mankind. (al-Qamar) So their Ijma' is proof: for if their Ijma' were not truth and proof, then it would be misguidance. So how can the misguided nation be the best of nations? And the author of al-Talwih said: Misguidance in some rulings based on error in ijtihad after exhausting one's effort does not negate that the believing scholars who follow the commands are the best of nations. And even if this is accepted, there is certainly no indication in the verse for the definitiveness of the Ijma' of the mujtahids of one era. (al-Qamar) / We will turn him to what he has turned to: i.e., We will make him a guardian of the misguidance he has turned to by leaving him to it in this world. (al-Qamar) Like opposing the Messenger etc.: for He threatened following other than the way of the believers just as He threatened opposing the Messenger with the obligation of Hellfire. So following other than the way of the believers is forbidden, so following the way of the believers is obligatory. Thus Ijma' is proof, for it is their way; since the way is what one chooses in speech and action. And one may say: Following other than the way of the believers is the same as opposing the Messenger, and the conceptual distinction in meaning is sufficient for the validity of conjunction, as in His saying: Obey Allah and obey the Messenger (al-Nisa 4:59) even though obedience to the Messenger is exactly obedience to Allah in external existence. In that case, there is no effect for establishing Ijma' from this verse, as said by the author of al-Tawdih. And the author of al-Talwih criticized him saying: Although the conjunction is valid, the way of the believers is general with no specification based on what the Messenger has brought, so there is no need for specification, and interpreting the speech to convey new benefit is preferable. (al-Qamar) Some of the Mu'tazila etc.: and also the Khawarij, and they are a small band of fools, not taken into account because they are later [sect] who cast doubt on the necessities of religion, like the Sophists [cast doubt] on rational necessities. (al-Sunbuli)
Source pages p. 629

Commentary
This passage, from the chapter on Ijma' in Noor al-Anwaar, states the ruling (hukm) of Ijma' (consensus) and its proofs. The author begins by asserting that Ijma' in legal matters provides certainty (yaqeen) and definitiveness (qat'iyyah) in principle, such that a denier of a ruling established by definitive Ijma' is considered a disbeliever (kafir). However, exceptions exist due to obstacles like 'ijma' sukuti' (silent consensus). The passage then provides Quranic proofs: (1) Quran 2:143 describing the Muslim community as a 'middle nation' (ummatan wasatan), interpreted as just, so their consensus is authoritative. (2) Quran 3:110 calling them 'the best nation', implying their consensus cannot be wrong. (3) Quran 4:115 warning against following 'other than the way of the believers', equating it to opposing the Messenger, thus establishing Ijma' as a definitive proof. The author then addresses objections from some Mu'tazila and Rawafid who deny Ijma' as a proof, dismissing them as a misguided few. The commentary (indicated by al-Qamar, al-Sunbuli, etc.) discusses nuances: the ruling applies only to legal matters, not worldly affairs like war; the certainty of Ijma' admits no contrary possibility; the takfir of deniers applies only if the matter is from the necessities of religion (dharuriyyat al-din) known to all; otherwise, a denier with a corrupt interpretation is not takfir. The passage also includes a rational proof: that all eras agree on the error of those opposing Ijma', and this certainty can only come from a decisive basis. The Hanafi position is that Ijma' is a qat'i proof, and its authority is from dharuriyyat al-din.

Key Terms
الوسط (al-wasat): Middle/just/balanced; used in 2:143 to describe the ummah.
سبيل المؤمنين (sabil al-mu'minin): The way/path of the believers; interpreted as their consensus on legal matters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a Quranic proof for Ijma' cited in this passage?
A) 2:143
B) 3:110
C) 4:115
D) 5:48

Key Takeaway
The authority of Ijma' is grounded in multiple Quranic verses and a rational proof, with verse 4:115 providing the strongest foundation.

The Requirement of a Motivating Evidence (Da'ee) for Ijma
Debating the necessity of a motivating factor for Ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi requirement of a da'ee for Ijma, identify its permissible sources (khabar al-wahid and qiyas), and evaluate the opposing view against Hanafi proofs.

Core Idea
Ijma must be based on a prior evidence; even a zanni source suffices, and Ijma elevates it to certainty.

Can Ijma occur spontaneously without any prior evidence? The Hanafi school insists that a motivating factor (da'ee) is essential, and that this da'ee may be a zanni source like a solitary hadith or analogy. This lesson unpacks the dispute, provides proof for the Hanafi position, and illustrates with concrete examples from the sources.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core dispute
Two opposing views: some say Ijma can occur without any da'ee (by divine inspiration or necessary knowledge), while the Hanafi position (declared al-mukhtar and al-asahh) requires a da'ee.
The da'ee is a shari' evidence that prompts the mujtahidun to reach consensus.
2
State the Hanafi position and its proof
The Hanafis argue that issuing a fatwa (the outcome of Ijma) without shari' evidence is haram, and it is impossible for all scholars to agree without a cause. Therefore a da'ee is necessary.
The proof is a rational argument (qiyas jaliy) combining legal principle and normal human behavior.
3
Examine the sources of da'ee
The da'ee can be from khabar al-wahid (solitary report) or qiyas (analogy). The text gives examples: Ijma on not selling food before possession (hadith), and Ijma on riba in rice (qiyas on six items).
These are zanni (probable) sources; Ijma renders the ruling qat'i.
4
Analyze the opposing view and Hanafi response
Opponents argue that if a da'ee is required, Ijma becomes superfluous. The Hanafi response: the benefit of Ijma is to transform a zanni ruling into a certain one, not to create a ruling from nothing.
Thus Ijma has a distinct epistemic function.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم إنهم اختلفوا في أن الإجماع هل يشترط في انعقاده أن يكون له داعٍ مقدّم عليه من دليل ظني أو ينعقد فجأةً بلا دليل باعث عليه بإلهام وتوفيق من الله بأن يخلق الله فيهم علمًا ضروريًا ويوفقهم لاختيار الصواب؟ فقيل: لا يشترط له الداعي، والأصح المختار أنه لا بد له من داع على ما قال المصنف : قد يكون من أخبار الآحاد والقياس، أمّا أخبار الآحاد فكإجماعهم على عدم جواز بيع الطعام قبل القبض والداعي إليه قوله عليه السلام: "لا تبيعوا الطعام قبل القبض"، وأما القياس فكإجماعهم على حرمة الربا في الأرز، والداعي إليه القياس على الأشياء الستة، وقيل: لا يجوز ذلك؛ إذ عند وجود الكتاب والسنة المشهورة لا يحتاج إلى الإجماع.
Then they differed: Is it required for the formation of Ijma that it has a preceding motivation from a speculative evidence, or does it occur suddenly without an evidence prompting it, by inspiration and divine favor from Allah, by Allah creating necessary knowledge in them and enabling them to choose the correct? So it was said: The motivation is not required. But the soundest and chosen view is that it must have a motivation, as the author said: It may be from solitary reports and analogy. As for solitary reports, like their consensus on the impermissibility of selling food before taking possession, the motivation being his statement (peace be upon him): "Do not sell food before taking possession." As for analogy, like their consensus on the prohibition of usury in rice, the motivation being analogy on the six items. And it was said: That is not permissible because when the Book and widespread Sunnah exist, there is no need for Ijma.
Source pages p. 631

Commentary
This passage is a usul dispute regarding the necessity of a motivating evidence (da'ee) for the formation of Ijma. The Hanafi position, presented as the soundest (mukhtar), is that Ijma cannot occur without a da'ee, but that da'ee can be from speculative (zanni) sources like khabar al-wahid (solitary report) or qiyas (analogy). The author provides examples: Ijma on not selling food before possession based on a hadith, and Ijma on usury in rice based on qiyas to the six ribawi items. A minority (including some Mu'tazila and Rawafid) claimed Ijma could occur without a da'ee. The text refutes this by citing two proofs: (1) issuing a fatwa without shari' evidence is haram, and (2) it is impossible for all scholars to unanimously agree without a cause, just as one cannot expect all people to agree on a single food without reason. The implication is that Ijma's primary benefit is to elevate a ruling from zanni to qat'i (certain), not to create a ruling from nothing.

Key Terms
داع (da'ee): The motivating evidence or basis that prompts the mujtahidun to reach an Ijma.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahidun of an era on a shari' ruling.
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith transmitted by one or a few narrators, not reaching tawatur, which gives probable (zanni) knowledge.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction from an original ruling to a new case based on shared 'illah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in Hanafi usul, what is the ruling on the requirement of a da'ee for Ijma?
A) It is not required.
B) It is required and must be from a qat'i source.
C) It is required but can be from a zanni source.
D) It is required only for matters of worship.

Key Takeaway
Ijma requires a prior evidence (da'ee), which may be from zanni sources; Ijma's role is to elevate the ruling to certainty.

Transmission of Ijma: Mutawatir vs. Ahad
Explaining the epistemological weight of differently transmitted Ijma

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mutawatir and ahad transmission of Ijma and apply the Hanafi rule that ahad Ijma obligates action despite being zanni.

Core Idea
Ijma transmitted via ahad obligates action but not certainty — akin to a solitary hadith.

This lesson categorizes the epistemological weight of Ijma based on its transmission method. The Hanafi school treats Ijma reported by a single chain as binding for action but not for certainty, drawing an analogy from solitary hadith reports. A key dispute with Imam al-Ghazali highlights the underlying usul principles.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two transmission modes
Recognize that Ijma can be transmitted either by tawatur (mass transmission at every generation) or by ahad (solitary reports). Tawatur yields certain knowledge and action; ahad yields only action.
The phrase 'Ijma of every era' refers to tawatur, not technical Ijma.
2
Understand the analogy to Sunnah
The text analogizes ahad Ijma to khabar al-wahid (solitary hadith): both obligate action but do not provide certainty.
This analogy is foundational to the Hanafi argument.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof (qiyas awwalawi)
The proof is a fortiori: if a zanni report (khabar al-wahid) obligates action, then a qat'i matter (Ijma) when transmitted via ahad is more deserving of obligating action.
This is a logical argument, not a textual one.
4
Recognize the opposing view
Imam al-Ghazali and some Hanafis argue that a qat'i matter loses its force when transmitted weakly, so ahad Ijma should not even obligate action.
The opposing view is based on the principle that certainty cannot be transmitted by non-certain means.
5
Determine the practical difference
The thamarah al-khilaf: a single reliable report of Ijma is accepted as binding by Hanafis, but not by al-Ghazali.
This affects fatwa and judicial decisions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم بين المصنف بالله أنه لا بد لنقل الإجماع أيضاً من الإجماع، فقال: وإذا انتقل إلينا إجماع السلف بإجماع كل عصر على نقله كان كنقل الحديث المتواتر، فيكون موجبًا للعلم والعمل قطعًا كإجماعهم على كون القرآن كتاب الله تعالى، وفرضية الصلاة وغيرها. كفرضية صوم رمضان وإذا انتقل إلينا بالأفراد كان كنقل السنة بالآحاد فإنه يوجب العمل دون العلم، مثل خبر الآحاد كقول عبيدة السلماني: اجتمع الصحابة على محافظة الأربع. ثم قال: القياس على إلخ أي قياس الأرز على الأشياء الستة، ثم أجمعوا على هذا القياس، فصار القياس بمعاضدة الإجماع قطعيًا. (القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ فهذا القول سبب داع إلى هذا الإجماع. (القمر) وقيل: القائل صاحب "التوضيح". (القمر) لا يحتاج إلى الإجماع: بل يكون الإجماع لغوا عرفا، فإنه لا يفيد حينئذ إلا التأكيد كما في النصوص المتعاضدة على حكم واحد والتأكيد ليس مقصود أصلي وقال صاحب "التلويح": إنه لا معنى للنزاع في جواز كون السند قطعيًا؛ لأنه إن أريد أنه لا يقع اتفاق مجتهدي عصر على حكم ثابت بدليل قطعي فظاهر البطلان، وإن أريد أنه لا يثبت الحكم فلا يتصوّر نزاع؛ لأن إثبات ما هو ثابت محال. (القمر) بإجماع إلخ المراد به تواتر كل عصر وليس المراد به الإجماع المصطلح (القمر) بالأفراد: أي بنقل الآحاد من دون الوصول إلى حد التواتر بأن روى ثقة أن الصحابة لهم أجمعوا على كذا. (القمر) فإنه يوجب إلخ فإن الإجماع حجة قطعية، والأمر القطعي إذا نقل بالأحاد صار معمولا به.(القمر) فإنه يوجب العمل إلخ: خلافا للغزالي الإمام، حجة الإسلام قدس سره وبعض الحنفية، ودليلنا نقل الظني كالخبر المأوّل مثلاً موجب للعمل قطعًا، فالقطعي المنقول آحادًا الذي هو الإجماع أولى بأن يوجب العمل.(السنبلي) مثل خبر الآحاد فإنه معمول به ولا يوجب العلم. (القمر) عبيدة السلماني إلخ كذا سُطر في "كشف "المنار" وقال بعض شراح "التحرير": هكذا يورد المشائخ، والله تعالى أعلم. كذا في الصبح الصادق (القمر) اجتمع كذا في التيسير نقلا عن بعض شروح "التحرير". (المحشي) على محافظة الأربع أي عدم تركها على كل حال.(القمر)
Then the author explained that the transmission of Ijma also requires Ijma. He said: If the Ijma of the predecessors is transmitted to us by the Ijma of every era upon its transmission, it is like the transmission of mutawatir hadith, thus it necessitates certain knowledge and action, like their Ijma that the Quran is the Book of Allah, and the obligation of prayer, etc., like the obligation of fasting Ramadan. And if it is transmitted to us by individuals, it is like the transmission of the Sunnah by solitary reports, so it necessitates action but not knowledge, like the solitary report from Ubaydah al-Sulmani: 'The Companions agreed upon preserving the four.'
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage establishes the epistemological classification of transmitted Ijma. If the Ijma of the Companions (or early generations) has been transmitted by multiple chains of narration at every generation (tawatur), it yields certain knowledge (ilm) and requires both belief and action. Examples include the Ijma that the Quran is Allah's Word and the obligatory nature of Salat and Sawm. If, however, the Ijma is reported by a single chain or individual (ahad), it only obligates action (amal) without producing certainty. The text cites the report of Ubaydah al-Sulmani that the Companions agreed on 'preserving the four' (likely the four rak'ahs of prayer). The commentary notes disagreement: Imam al-Ghazali and some Hanafis argued that ahad reports of Ijma do not even obligate action, but the Hanafi position (based on the analogy that zanni reports obligate action, so qat'i reports are even more deserving) is that they do obligate action. The discussion also includes technical points: transmission 'by the Ijma of every era' means tawatur across generations, not the technical Ijma; and 'by individuals' means a report from a trustworthy narrator that the Sahaba agreed on something.

Key Terms
تواتر (tawatur): Mutawatir transmission: the report is transmitted by such a large number that collusion on a lie is impossible, yielding certain knowledge.
آحاد (ahad): Ahad transmission: report transmitted by one or a few chains, not reaching tawatur, giving probable knowledge but not certainty.
إجماع (ijma): Consensus of the mujtahidun; here also used for the transmission of Ijma across generations (tawatur).
خبر الآحاد (khabar al-wahid): A solitary report that does not reach tawatur; it is zanni and acted upon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the Ijma of the Companions is reported by a single trustworthy narrator, what is its ruling?
A) It is rejected and not acted upon.
B) It gives certain knowledge and must be believed.
C) It obligates action but does not give certain knowledge.
D) It gives certain knowledge but is not acted upon.

Key Takeaway
The transmission mode of Ijma determines its epistemological force: mutawatir gives certainty, ahad gives only obligation to act.

Transmission of Ijma: Certainty and Actionability
Explaining the transmission levels of Ijma and the Hanafi rule on actionability.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between mutawatir and ahad transmission of ijma and apply the Hanafi rule that ahad-transmitted ijma obligates action but not certainty.

Core Idea
Ijma via tawatur gives certainty and requires belief; via ahad gives action without certainty.

This lesson explores how the consensus of the Salaf reaches us. The Hanafi school classifies transmission of ijma into tawatur (mass transmission) and ahad (individual reports). The ruling mirrors that of hadith. We examine the evidence and a key dispute with Imam al-Ghazali on whether a definitive matter transmitted via ahad can be actioned.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two modes of transmission
Understand that ijma can be transmitted via tawatur (each generation transmitting the consensus) or via ahad (a single trustworthy report).
2
Compare to hadith transmission
Recognize the analogy: mutawatir ijma gives certainty (like mutawatir hadith), ahad ijma gives action but not certainty (like ahad hadith).
3
Analyze the example of 'Ubayda al-Salmani
This is an ahad report of Sahaba consensus; it is acted upon but does not produce certainty.
The report states 'the Companions agreed on preserving the four (rak'ahs).'
4
Evaluate the Ghazali objection
Understand why al-Ghazali and some Hanafis argued that a definitive matter transmitted via ahad does not necessitate action, and the Hanafi response that even probabilistic transmission necessitates action.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإجماع
بيان حكم الإجماع
وأما القياس فكإجماعهم على حرمة الربا في الأرز، والداعي إليه القياس على الأشياء الستة، وفي قوله: قد يكون إشارة إلى أن الداعي قد يكون من الكتاب أيضا كإجماعهم على حرمة الجدات وبنات البنات؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿حُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْكُمْ أُمَّهَاتُكُمْ وَبَنَاتُكُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٢٣)
وقيل: لا يجوز ذلك؛ إذ عند وجود الكتاب والسنة المشهورة لا يحتاج إلى الإجماع. ثم بين المصنف بالله أنه لا بد لنقل الإجماع أيضاً من الإجماع، فقال: وإذا انتقل إلينا إجماع السلف بإجماع كل عصر على نقله كان كنقل الحديث المتواتر، فيكون موجبًا للعلم والعمل قطعًا كإجماعهم على كون القرآن كتاب الله تعالى، وفرضية الصلاة وغيرها. كفرضية صوم رمضان وإذا انتقل إلينا بالأفراد كان كنقل السنة بالآحاد فإنه يوجب العمل دون العلم، مثل خبر الآحاد كقول عبيدة السلماني: اجتمع الصحابة على محافظة الأربع.
القياس على إلخ أي قياس الأرز على الأشياء الستة، ثم أجمعوا على هذا القياس، فصار القياس بمعاضدة الإجماع قطعيًا. (القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ فهذا القول سبب داع إلى هذا الإجماع. (القمر) وقيل: القائل صاحب "التوضيح". (القمر) لا يحتاج إلى الإجماع: بل يكون الإجماع لغوا عرفا، فإنه لا يفيد حينئذ إلا التأكيد كما في النصوص المتعاضدة على حكم واحد والتأكيد ليس مقصود أصلي وقال صاحب "التلويح": إنه لا معنى للنزاع في جواز كون السند قطعيًا؛ لأنه إن أريد أنه لا يقع اتفاق مجتهدي عصر على حكم ثابت بدليل قطعي فظاهر البطلان، وإن أريد أنه لا يثبت الحكم فلا يتصوّر نزاع؛ لأن إثبات ما هو ثابت محال. (القمر) بإجماع إلخ المراد به تواتر كل عصر وليس المراد به الإجماع المصطلح (القمر) بالأفراد: أي بنقل الآحاد من دون الوصول إلى حد التواتر بأن روى ثقة أن الصحابة لهم أجمعوا على كذا. (القمر)
فإنه يوجب إلخ فإن الإجماع حجة قطعية، والأمر القطعي إذا نقل بالأحاد صار معمولا به. (القمر) فإنه يوجب العمل إلخ: خلافا للغزالي الإمام، حجة الإسلام قدس سره وبعض الحنفية، ودليلنا نقل الظني كالخبر المأوّل مثلاً موجب للعمل قطعًا، فالقطعي المنقول آحادًا الذي هو الإجماع أولى بأن يوجب العمل. (السنبلي) مثل خبر الآحاد فإنه معمول به ولا يوجب العلم. (القمر) عبيدة السلماني إلخ كذا سُطر في "كشف المنار" وقال بعض شراح "التحرير": هكذا يورد المشائخ، والله تعالى أعلم. كذا في الصبح الصادق (القمر) اجتمع كذا في التيسير نقلا عن بعض شروح "التحرير". (المحشي) على محافظة الأربع أي عدم تركها على كل حال. (القمر)
باب الإجماع
بيان مراتب أهل الإجماع
قبل الظهر، وتحريم نكاح الأخت في عدّة الأخت، وتوكيد المهر بالخلوة الصحيحة،
و لم يتعرّض لتمثيله بالحديث المشهور؛ إذ لا فرق بينه وبين المتواتر إلا عدم اشتهاره في قرن الصحابة منه، وهذا لم يستقم ههنا؛ لأن الإجماع لم يكن في زمن الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم وإنما يكون في زمن الصحابة، فبعده ليس إلا آحاد أو متواتر.
إجماع الصحابة
ثم هو على مراتب أي الإجماع في نفسه مع قطع النظر عن نقله له مراتب في القوة، والضعف واليقين والظن
فالأقوى إجماع الصحابة نصا مثل أن يقولوا جميعًا: أجمعنا على كذا، فإنه مثل الآية والخبر المتواتر حتى يكفّر جاحده، ومنه الإجماع على خلافة أبي بكر أي في إفادة اليقين
ثم الذي نص البعض وسكت الباقون من الصحابة، وهو المسمّى بالإجماع السكوني، ولا يكفر جاحده
بالخلوة الصحيحة هي أن لا يوجد فيها المانع للوطء بالمنكوحة حسيا كان كالمرض المانع من الوطء، وشرعيًا كصوم رمضان، أو طبعيًا كالاستحاضة، كذا في جامع العلوم (القمر) على مراتب إلخ الحاصل أن الأعلى إجماع الصحابة نصاً بحيث يكفّر جاحده، ثم إجماعهم السكوتي، ثم إجماع من بعدهم بحيث لم يسبق فيه خلاف، ثم إجماعهم وقد استقر خلاف سابق، هذا ما قاله الإمام فخر الإسلام، ووجهه الذي بينه العلماء مذكور في الكتب الطويلة لا يحتمله هذا المختصر، والله تعالى أعلم. (السنبلي) والظن وما وقع في مسير "الدائر" مقام الظن لفظ "الشك" فمِن زلة القلم؛ إذ ليس إجماع يفيد الشك، بل الإجماع الأنزل رتبة كخبر الواحد يفيد الظن لا العلم ويوجب العمل. (القمر) نصا إلخ القطعيته بالإجماع؛ إذ لم يُعتبر خلاف منكره (فتح الغفار: ٣٥٥) على خلافة إلخ كذا قال الشيخ ابن الهمام في "التحرير". (القمر)
على خلافة لأن المهاجرين والأنصار قد اتفقوا على خلافة أبي بكر قبل دفن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالإجماع السكوتي كإجماع الصحابة له على قتال مانع الزكاة، فإن أكثر الصحابة له قد قالوا به، وبعضهم كانوا ساكتين مسلمين. (القمر) ولا يكفّر جاحده بل يُضلّل جاحده لوجود خلاف الشافعي الله فيه كما قد مرّ
كما أن موجب العام قطعي عندنا ولا يكفّر جاحده لخلاف الشافعي له فيه، فإن موجب العام عنده ظني. (القمر)
Chapter of Consensus. Explanation of the ruling of Consensus. As for analogy, it is like their consensus on the prohibition of riba in rice, and the cause for it is analogy on the six items. And in his statement: 'it may be' is an indication that the cause may also be from the Book, like their consensus on the prohibition of grandmothers and daughters of daughters, due to His statement: 'Forbidden to you are your mothers and your daughters' (4:23). And it was said: that is not permissible, because when the Book and well-known Sunnah are present, there is no need for consensus. Then the author explained that for the transmission of consensus also, consensus is necessary. He said: And if consensus of the predecessors reaches us through the consensus of every age upon its transmission, it is like the transmission of mutawatir hadith, thus it necessitates certainty and action definitively, like their consensus that the Qur'an is the Book of Allah and the obligation of prayer etc., like the obligation of fasting Ramadan. And if it reaches us through individuals, it is like the transmission of sunnah through ahad reports, that it necessitates action without certainty, like ahad reports, like the statement of 'Ubayda al-Salmani: The Companions agreed on preserving the four. 'Analogy on etc.' meaning analogy of rice on the six items, then they agreed on this analogy, so the analogy became definitive due to the support of consensus. (Qamar) 'Due to His statement etc.' so this statement is a cause leading to this consensus. (Qamar) 'And it was said': the speaker is the author of al-Tawdih. (Qamar) 'Does not need consensus': rather consensus would be redundant customarily, because it then yields only emphasis, as in texts mutually supporting one ruling, and emphasis is not the primary purpose. And the author of al-Talwih said: There is no meaning to dispute over whether the chain can be definitive; if it means that agreement of the mujtahids of an age cannot occur on a ruling established by a definitive proof, that is obviously false; if it means that the ruling is not established, then no dispute is conceivable; because establishing what is already established is impossible. (Qamar) 'By consensus etc.' what is meant is tawatur of every age, not the terminological consensus. (Qamar) 'By individuals': i.e., by transmission of ahad without reaching the level of tawatur, by a trustworthy person reporting that the Companions agreed on something. (Qamar) 'It necessitates etc.' then consensus is a definitive proof, and a definitive matter when transmitted through ahad becomes operative. (Qamar) 'It necessitates action etc.' contrary to Imam al-Ghazali and some Hanafis; our evidence is that a probabilistic transmission like a ta'wil-ed report necessitates action definitively, so a definitive [report] transmitted as ahad, which is consensus, is more appropriate to necessitate action. (Sanbali) Like ahad reports: it is acted upon but does not give certainty. (Qamar) 'Ubayda al-Salmani etc.' as recorded in Kashf al-Manar, and some commentators of al-Tahrir said: thus the mashayikh relate it, and Allah knows best. In al-Subh al-Sadiq (Qamar) 'Agreed' as in al-Taysir quoting some commentaries of al-Tahrir. (Muhashshi) 'On preserving the four': i.e., never abandoning them. (Qamar) Chapter of Consensus. Explanation of the ranks of the people of Consensus. Before Zuhr, prohibition of marrying a sister during the 'idda of her sister, confirmation of mahr by valid seclusion. And he did not exemplify it with the mashhur hadith, since there is no difference between it and mutawatir except lack of fame in the generation of the Companions, and this is not correct here because consensus did not exist in the time of the Prophet (PBUH), but rather in the time of the Companions; after that it is only ahad or mutawatir. Consensus of the Companions. Then it has levels, i.e., consensus in itself, regardless of its transmission, has levels of strength, weakness, certainty, and probability. The strongest is the explicit consensus of the Companions, like when they all say: we agreed on this, then it is like the verse and mutawatir report such that its denier is deemed a disbeliever; and among it is the consensus on the caliphate of Abu Bakr, i.e., in giving certainty. Then that which some stated explicitly and the rest of the Companions remained silent, which is called silent consensus, and its denier is not deemed a disbeliever. 'By valid seclusion' is that which does not have a barrier to intercourse with the wife, whether sensory like illness preventing intercourse, or legal like Ramadan fast, or natural like istihada, as in Jami' al-Ulum. (Qamar) 'On levels etc.' the summary: the highest is explicit consensus of the Companions such that its denier is deemed a disbeliever, then their silent consensus, then consensus of those after them where no prior disagreement occurred, then consensus after a prior disagreement had been settled. This is what Imam Fakhr al-Islam said, and its explanation by the scholars is mentioned in lengthy books; this concise work cannot accommodate it. Allah knows best. (Sanbali) 'And probability' and what appeared in the margins of al-Da'ir in place of 'probability' the word 'doubt' is a slip of the pen; for there is no consensus that gives doubt, but the lowest rank of consensus is like a single report, giving probability not certainty, and necessitates action. (Qamar) 'Explicitly etc.' its definitiveness is due to consensus, since the opposition of its denier is not considered. (Fath al-Ghaffar: 355) 'On the caliphate etc.' as stated by Ibn al-Humam in al-Tahrir. (Qamar) 'On the caliphate' because the Muhajirun and Ansar agreed on the caliphate of Abu Bakr before burying the Messenger of Allah (PBUH) by silent consensus, like the consensus of the Companions on fighting the refusers of Zakat, for most of the Companions spoke [in favor] and some remained silent accepting. (Qamar) 'And its denier is not deemed a disbeliever' but rather its denier is deemed an innovator due to the existence of the opposition of al-Shafi'i, as has passed. Just as the implication of a general term is definitive according to us, but its denier is not deemed a disbeliever due to the opposition of al-Shafi'i, for the implication of the general term is probabilistic according to him. (Qamar)
Source pages p. 632

Commentary
This passage from the Hanafi usul text Noor al-Anwar discusses the nature and authority of Ijma (consensus). The author first explains that consensus can be established through analogy (qiyas), citing the example of the prohibition of riba in rice based on analogy to the six classical items, and also from explicit Quranic texts as a cause (dai). Then he addresses the transmission of consensus: if transmitted through the continuous consensus of each generation (tawatur), it gives certain knowledge and demands action; if transmitted through individual reports (ahad), it demands action but does not provide certainty. This is likened to mutawatir vs. ahad hadith. The text then delves into a dispute: some argue that if a ruling is already established by Quran and well-known Sunnah, consensus is unnecessary. The author refutes this by noting that consensus can still serve as reinforcement (ta'kid). A note from al-Talwih dismisses the dispute as meaningless. The passage also contrasts with Imam al-Ghazali and some Hanafis who argue that a definitive matter transmitted through ahad does not necessitate action; the Hanafi position, supported by the author, affirms that it does. The second part of the passage categorizes the levels (maratib) of consensus itself, independent of its transmission. The strongest is the explicit consensus of the Companions, which is like a Quranic verse or mutawatir report—its denier is deemed a disbeliever (kafir). An example is the consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate. The next level is silent consensus (ijma sukti), where some Companions voice an opinion and others remain silent; its denier is not considered a disbeliever but is considered misguided (mudallal). The passage further distinguishes consensus of later generations with or without prior disagreement. The Hanafi view on 'amm (general term) is also invoked: the denier of a definitive 'amm is not declared a disbeliever because of the opposing view of al-Shafi'i, who considers 'amm probabilistic. This shows the Hanafi principle that takfir requires consensus that is explicit and uninterrupted.

Key Terms
الإجماع (al-Ijma'): Consensus of the mujtahids of an age on a religious ruling; a source of law that can be transmitted either via tawatur (giving certainty) or ahad (giving action).
المتواتر (al-Mutawatir): A transmission by a multitude that precludes collusion; it gives certain knowledge.
الآحاد (al-Ahad): Singular reports; transmission that does not reach the level of tawatur, giving probabilistic knowledge but still actionable.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a single trustworthy person reports that the Sahaba agreed on a ruling, which of the following is true?
A) This report constitutes certain knowledge of ijma.
B) This report must be acted upon but does not produce certainty.
C) This report is not valid because ijma requires tawatur.
D) This report is only valid if supported by a Quranic verse.

Key Takeaway
Ijma transmitted via ahad reports obligates action but not certainty, unlike mutawatir ijma which gives both.

Al-Ijma — Consensus
intermediate
8 min
Levels of Ijma: From Explicit Consensus to Silent Approval
Explaining the hierarchical levels of Ijma and the takfir consequences.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four levels of ijma in Hanafi usul and determine whether the denier of each level is considered a disbeliever or merely misguided.

Core Idea
Explicit Sahaba consensus is as definitive as Quran; silent consensus is binding but its denier is not excommunicated.

This lesson examines the hierarchical levels of ijma independent of transmission. The strongest is explicit consensus of the Sahaba, which gives certainty and excommunicates its denier. Below that is silent consensus, where some Sahaba spoke and others remained silent—its denier is not a disbeliever but is misguided. The passage also clarifies the role of legitimate ikhtilaf in preventing takfir, drawing an analogy with the definitive 'amm.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the four levels of ijma
The passage from Sanbali lists: (1) explicit consensus of Sahaba, (2) silent consensus of Sahaba, (3) consensus of later scholars without prior ikhtilaf, (4) consensus of later scholars after prior ikhtilaf has been settled.
Levels 3 and 4 are mentioned in the Sanbali commentary.
2
Identify the takfir implications
Denier of explicit Sahaba consensus is a kafir (like denier of mutawatir hadith). Denier of silent consensus is not a kafir but is considered an innovator (mudallal). This is because silent consensus does not carry the same certainty.
The text explicitly says 'yukaffar jahiduhu' for explicit and 'la yukaffar jahiduhu' for silent.
3
Analyze the example of caliphate and zakat
The consensus on Abu Bakr's caliphate was a silent consensus (the Muhajirun and Ansar agreed, with some silent). Similarly, the consensus on fighting the refusers of zakat was silent. The denier of these is not a kafir because of the existence of a prior differing opinion (al-Shafi'i's).
4
Connect to the principle of 'amm
The passage draws an analogy: the implication of a general term ('amm) is definitive (qat'i) in Hanafi usul, but its denier is not declared a disbeliever because of al-Shafi'i's opposing view that 'amm is probabilistic.
This shows that takfir is only applied when there is no legitimate ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الإجماع
بيان حكم الإجماع
وأما القياس فكإجماعهم على حرمة الربا في الأرز، والداعي إليه القياس على الأشياء الستة، وفي قوله: قد يكون إشارة إلى أن الداعي قد يكون من الكتاب أيضا كإجماعهم على حرمة الجدات وبنات البنات؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿حُرِّمَتْ عَلَيْكُمْ أُمَّهَاتُكُمْ وَبَنَاتُكُمْ﴾ (النساء: ٢٣)
وقيل: لا يجوز ذلك؛ إذ عند وجود الكتاب والسنة المشهورة لا يحتاج إلى الإجماع. ثم بين المصنف بالله أنه لا بد لنقل الإجماع أيضاً من الإجماع، فقال: وإذا انتقل إلينا إجماع السلف بإجماع كل عصر على نقله كان كنقل الحديث المتواتر، فيكون موجبًا للعلم والعمل قطعًا كإجماعهم على كون القرآن كتاب الله تعالى، وفرضية الصلاة وغيرها. كفرضية صوم رمضان وإذا انتقل إلينا بالأفراد كان كنقل السنة بالآحاد فإنه يوجب العمل دون العلم، مثل خبر الآحاد كقول عبيدة السلماني: اجتمع الصحابة على محافظة الأربع.
القياس على إلخ أي قياس الأرز على الأشياء الستة، ثم أجمعوا على هذا القياس، فصار القياس بمعاضدة الإجماع قطعيًا. (القمر) لقوله تعالى إلخ فهذا القول سبب داع إلى هذا الإجماع. (القمر) وقيل: القائل صاحب "التوضيح". (القمر) لا يحتاج إلى الإجماع: بل يكون الإجماع لغوا عرفا، فإنه لا يفيد حينئذ إلا التأكيد كما في النصوص المتعاضدة على حكم واحد والتأكيد ليس مقصود أصلي وقال صاحب "التلويح": إنه لا معنى للنزاع في جواز كون السند قطعيًا؛ لأنه إن أريد أنه لا يقع اتفاق مجتهدي عصر على حكم ثابت بدليل قطعي فظاهر البطلان، وإن أريد أنه لا يثبت الحكم فلا يتصوّر نزاع؛ لأن إثبات ما هو ثابت محال. (القمر) بإجماع إلخ المراد به تواتر كل عصر وليس المراد به الإجماع المصطلح (القمر) بالأفراد: أي بنقل الآحاد من دون الوصول إلى حد التواتر بأن روى ثقة أن الصحابة لهم أجمعوا على كذا. (القمر)
فإنه يوجب إلخ فإن الإجماع حجة قطعية، والأمر القطعي إذا نقل بالأحاد صار معمولا به. (القمر) فإنه يوجب العمل إلخ: خلافا للغزالي الإمام، حجة الإسلام قدس سره وبعض الحنفية، ودليلنا نقل الظني كالخبر المأوّل مثلاً موجب للعمل قطعًا، فالقطعي المنقول آحادًا الذي هو الإجماع أولى بأن يوجب العمل. (السنبلي) مثل خبر الآحاد فإنه معمول به ولا يوجب العلم. (القمر) عبيدة السلماني إلخ كذا سُطر في "كشف المنار" وقال بعض شراح "التحرير": هكذا يورد المشائخ، والله تعالى أعلم. كذا في الصبح الصادق (القمر) اجتمع كذا في التيسير نقلا عن بعض شروح "التحرير". (المحشي) على محافظة الأربع أي عدم تركها على كل حال. (القمر)
باب الإجماع
بيان مراتب أهل الإجماع
قبل الظهر، وتحريم نكاح الأخت في عدّة الأخت، وتوكيد المهر بالخلوة الصحيحة،
و لم يتعرّض لتمثيله بالحديث المشهور؛ إذ لا فرق بينه وبين المتواتر إلا عدم اشتهاره في قرن الصحابة منه، وهذا لم يستقم ههنا؛ لأن الإجماع لم يكن في زمن الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم وإنما يكون في زمن الصحابة، فبعده ليس إلا آحاد أو متواتر.
إجماع الصحابة
ثم هو على مراتب أي الإجماع في نفسه مع قطع النظر عن نقله له مراتب في القوة، والضعف واليقين والظن
فالأقوى إجماع الصحابة نصا مثل أن يقولوا جميعًا: أجمعنا على كذا، فإنه مثل الآية والخبر المتواتر حتى يكفّر جاحده، ومنه الإجماع على خلافة أبي بكر أي في إفادة اليقين
ثم الذي نص البعض وسكت الباقون من الصحابة، وهو المسمّى بالإجماع السكوني، ولا يكفر جاحده
بالخلوة الصحيحة هي أن لا يوجد فيها المانع للوطء بالمنكوحة حسيا كان كالمرض المانع من الوطء، وشرعيًا كصوم رمضان، أو طبعيًا كالاستحاضة، كذا في جامع العلوم (القمر) على مراتب إلخ الحاصل أن الأعلى إجماع الصحابة نصاً بحيث يكفّر جاحده، ثم إجماعهم السكوتي، ثم إجماع من بعدهم بحيث لم يسبق فيه خلاف، ثم إجماعهم وقد استقر خلاف سابق، هذا ما قاله الإمام فخر الإسلام، ووجهه الذي بينه العلماء مذكور في الكتب الطويلة لا يحتمله هذا المختصر، والله تعالى أعلم. (السنبلي) والظن وما وقع في مسير "الدائر" مقام الظن لفظ "الشك" فمِن زلة القلم؛ إذ ليس إجماع يفيد الشك، بل الإجماع الأنزل رتبة كخبر الواحد يفيد الظن لا العلم ويوجب العمل. (القمر) نصا إلخ القطعيته بالإجماع؛ إذ لم يُعتبر خلاف منكره (فتح الغفار: ٣٥٥) على خلافة إلخ كذا قال الشيخ ابن الهمام في "التحرير". (القمر)
على خلافة لأن المهاجرين والأنصار قد اتفقوا على خلافة أبي بكر قبل دفن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم بالإجماع السكوتي كإجماع الصحابة له على قتال مانع الزكاة، فإن أكثر الصحابة له قد قالوا به، وبعضهم كانوا ساكتين مسلمين. (القمر) ولا يكفّر جاحده بل يُضلّل جاحده لوجود خلاف الشافعي الله فيه كما قد مرّ
كما أن موجب العام قطعي عندنا ولا يكفّر جاحده لخلاف الشافعي له فيه، فإن موجب العام عنده ظني. (القمر)
